```markdown
- PsyToolkit Corsi Block task page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/corsi.html
- PsyToolkit Corsi Block run page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_corsi.html
- PsyToolkit Backward Corsi task page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/backward_corsi.html
- PsyToolkit Backward Corsi run page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_backward_corsi.html

## Updating and complex working memory labs (strong “lab feel”)
- PsyToolkit 2-Back task page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/nback2.html
- PsyToolkit 2-Back run page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_nback2.html
- PsyToolkit Automated Operation Span task page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/aospan.html
- PsyToolkit Automated Operation Span run page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_aospan.html
- PsyToolkit Retro-Cue visual working memory task page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/retrocue.html
- PsyToolkit Retro-Cue run page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_retrocue.html
- PsyToolkit Digit Symbol Substitution task page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/digit_substitution.html
- PsyToolkit Digit Symbol Substitution run page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_digit_substitution.html

## Memory decay and interference labs (adjust parameters, then compare outcomes)
- Hanover Brown–Peterson short-term memory interference lab: https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/BrownPeterson.html
- Hanover Partial Report (Sperling iconic memory) lab: https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/partialReport.html

## Serial position and false memory labs (high-yield for intro psych)
- Hanover Serial Position lab: https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/SerialPosition.html
- Hanover DRM False Memory lab: https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/DRMfalseMemory.html

## Memory span with adjustable method settings (Hanover)
- Hanover Memory Span lab (staircase procedure): https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/span.html

## Optional student-facing “Memory Games” task (results at end)
- TestMyBrain Memory Games direct task page: https://studies.testmybrain.org/m2c2/?study=m2c2
```

### Block 38 (lang=markdown | source=md | block 38)

```markdown
---
title: "PSY-132 Interactive Teaching Labs (Free Only): Cognition"
course: "PSY-132 Introductory Psychology"
type: "resource_links"
scope: "teaching_interactive_labs_only_free"
topics:
  - topic_number: 12
    topic_name: "Cognition"
created: 2025-12-31
---

## Selection rationale
- These links run in a web browser and do not require plugins or paid accounts
- These links produce observable outcomes you can treat as data, such as reaction time, accuracy, or choice patterns
- These links support clean intro-psych debriefs about information processing limits, cognitive control, and decision making

## Core lab hubs (bookmark these and reuse all semester)
- PsyToolkit Experiment Library (50+ browser-run cognitive tasks): https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/
- Hanover Cognition Laboratory Experiments, HTML5/JS set (parameters can be adjusted): https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/cognition.html

## Lab set A: Attention and cognitive control (reaction time and errors)

### Interference and selective attention
- PsyToolkit Stroop overview: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/stroop.html
- PsyToolkit Stroop run page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_stroop.html
- Hanover Stroop (HTML5 version with results reporting): https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/stroop.html

### Distractor interference and executive attention
- PsyToolkit Flanker overview: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/flanker.html
- PsyToolkit Flanker run page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_flanker.html
- PsyToolkit Flanker arrows overview: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/flanker_arrows.html

### Switching costs and cognitive flexibility
- PsyToolkit Task Switching overview: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/taskswitching.html
- PsyToolkit Task Switching run page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_taskswitching.html
- PsyToolkit Multitasking overview: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/multitasking.html
- PsyToolkit Multitasking run page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_multitasking.html

### Response inhibition and “stopping” a prepared action
- PsyToolkit Go/No-go overview: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/go-no-go.html
- PsyToolkit Go/No-go run page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_go-no-go.html
- PsyToolkit Stop-Signal overview: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/stopsignal.html
- PsyToolkit Stop-Signal run page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_stopsignal.html

## Lab set B: Bottlenecks and limits (temporal attention, divided attention)

### Attentional blink (the “second target disappears” effect)
- PsyToolkit Attentional Blink overview: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/ab.html
- PsyToolkit Attentional Blink run page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_ab.html
- Hanover Attentional Blink (HTML5/JS): https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/attnBlink.html

### Divided attention as a manipulable lab (cognitive load)
- Hanover Dual Task experiment (tracking plus target detection): https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/dualTask.html

## Lab set C: Visual search and mental imagery (problem solving by manipulation)

### Visual search (set size effects you can graph)
- PsyToolkit Visual Search overview: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/search.html
- PsyToolkit Visual Search run page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_search.html

### Mental rotation (processing time increases with rotation angle)
- Hanover Mental Rotation (HTML5/JS): https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/mentRot.html

## Lab set D: Reasoning and decision making (choice patterns)

### Rule testing and confirmation bias traps
- Philosophy Experiments, Wason Selection Task (Q1): https://www.philosophyexperiments.com/wason/Default.aspx
- Philosophy Experiments, Wason Selection Task (Q2): https://www.philosophyexperiments.com/wason/Default2.aspx
- Philosophy Experiments, Wason Selection Task (Q3): https://www.philosophyexperiments.com/wason/Default3.aspx

### Probabilistic reasoning under intuition pressure
- Monty Hall interactive simulator: https://montyhall.io/

## Reasoning and teaching ideas (practical, low-friction)

### The simplest “online lab” workflow that stays intro-friendly
- Pick one task from Lab set A and run it as a whole-class demo first, then let students run individually
- Use one dependent variable only for the first pass, such as mean reaction time or total errors
- Ask students to submit a single number and a screenshot of their results page in the LMS

### Fast debrief questions that force a lab mindset
- What is the independent variable, and what values did it take
- What is the dependent variable, and how was it measured
- What alternative explanations exist, such as practice effects, device differences, distractions, or misunderstanding instructions
- What pattern would you predict if we changed difficulty, time pressure, or the proportion of trials

### Two ready-to-run 50-minute class formats
- Station rotation format: Use Stroop, Flanker, Task Switching, and Monty Hall as four stations, then do a whole-class synthesis comparing “where cognition breaks”
- Bottleneck format: Use Attentional Blink plus Dual Task, then treat both as evidence that attention is limited and not a single pool

### Easy ways to connect Cognition back to Statistics without adding work
- Compare two conditions as a difference score, such as congruent minus incongruent reaction time in Stroop
- Graph the class distribution and discuss skew, outliers, and measurement noise
- Use the same dataset later as practice for confidence intervals or randomization tests
```

### Block 39 (lang=markdown | source=md | block 39)

```markdown
---
title: "PSY-132 Interactive Teaching Labs (Free Only): Intelligence"
course: "PSY-132 Introductory Psychology"
type: "resource_links"
scope: "teaching_interactive_labs_only_free"
topics:
  - topic_number: 13
    topic_name: "Intelligence"
created: 2025-12-31
---

## Selection rationale
- These labs are free to run for students in a browser, except where explicitly labeled as an optional app-based lab
- These labs produce concrete outputs you can treat as data, such as reaction time, accuracy, span length, or number correct
- These labs support intro-psych debriefs about what intelligence tests actually measure, how measurement error shows up, and why “one score” is always a simplification

## Instructor framing that keeps this academically clean
- Treat results as demonstrations of measurement and individual differences, not as diagnosis or placement
- Use anonymous or coded IDs for submissions, especially if you plan to aggregate class results
- Use at least two different task types so students see that “intelligence” is not one skill

## Core lab hubs (bookmark and reuse)
- PsyToolkit Experiment Library (browser-run experiments with no plugins): https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/
- Hanover Cognition Laboratory Experiments, HTML5/JS hub (adjustable parameters): https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/cognition.html

## Lab station set (recommended): Build intelligence from components

### Station A: Processing speed and visual scanning
- PsyToolkit Digit Symbol Substitution Test (DSST) overview: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/digit_substitution.html
- PsyToolkit DSST run page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_digit_substitution.html

### Station B: Working memory capacity
- PsyToolkit Digit Span overview: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/digitspan.html
- PsyToolkit Digit Span run page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_digitspan.html

- PsyToolkit Automated Operation Span (O-Span) overview: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/aospan.html
- PsyToolkit O-Span run page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_aospan.html

### Station C: Spatial reasoning
- PsyToolkit Mental Rotation overview: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/mentalrotation.html
- PsyToolkit Mental Rotation run page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_mentalrotation.html

- Hanover Mental Rotation Experiment (HTML5/JS with adjustable settings): https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/mentRot.html

### Station D: Rule discovery and cognitive flexibility
- PsyToolkit WCST-inspired task overview: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/wcst.html
- PsyToolkit WCST-inspired run page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_wcst.html

### Station E: Verbal ability, with explicit fairness caveats
- OpenPsychometrics Vocabulary IQ Test (VIQT) start page: https://openpsychometrics.org/tests/VIQT/

## Optional composite lab (use only if you want to discuss what a single “IQ-like” number does and does not mean)
- OpenPsychometrics Full Scale IQ Test (FSIQ) start page: https://openpsychometrics.org/tests/FSIQ/
- OpenPsychometrics FSIQ results page (shows how they adjust results for the online sample): https://openpsychometrics.org/tests/FSIQ/results.php

## Optional app-based lab (still free, but not browser-based)
- UC Matrix Reasoning Task (UCMRT) overview article with app-download instructions: https://news.ucr.edu/articles/2018/10/29/uc-psychologists-devise-free-test-measuring-intelligence

## Teaching ideas that keep the activity “lab-like”

### Minimal-prep 50-minute class plan
- Run DSST and Mental Rotation as a whole-class warm-up so students understand the output
- Assign O-Span or Digit Span as the individual lab component
- End with a synthesis prompt where students map each task to a hypothesized ability component, such as speed, working memory, or spatial reasoning

### Data collection that stays lightweight
- Require only one metric per station, such as number correct, max span, or mean reaction time
- Use a single Google Form or Brightspace quiz item per station with one numeric field and one reflection field

### Debrief questions that force scientific thinking
- What is the dependent variable, and what did the task treat as “better performance”
- What nuisance variables could distort results, including device type, screen size, distractions, or misunderstanding instructions
- What would you change to improve validity if this were a real assessment study

### A high-yield concept demo that students remember
- Show “positive manifold” by asking whether students who score high on DSST also tend to score higher on span or rotation
- Use that pattern to motivate the idea of a general factor without claiming that any single student’s score is their “true intelligence”
```

### Block 40 (lang=markdown | source=md | block 40)

```markdown
---
title: "PSY-132 Interactive Teaching Labs (Free Only): Language"
course: "PSY-132 Introductory Psychology"
type: "resource_links"
scope: "teaching_interactive_labs_only_free"
topics:
  - topic_number: 14
    topic_name: "Language"
created: 2025-12-31
---

## Selection rationale
- These activities run in a browser and do not require paid access
- These activities behave like labs because students produce observable outcomes such as reaction time, accuracy, or structured perceptual judgments
- These activities support clean Intro Psych debriefs about bottom-up input, top-down expectations, and measurement error

## Quick setup notes for smooth teaching
- Plan for keyboards for at least one part of this topic because many tasks use keypress timing
- Use headphones for speech perception activities unless a specific activity recommends speakers
- Treat results as demonstrations of processes, not as diagnostics

## Core lab hubs you can reuse
- PsyToolkit experiment library: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/
- Hanover Cognition Laboratory Experiments, HTML5/JS hub: https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/cognition.html
- ISLE 2.0 Chapter 12 Speech Perception hub: https://isle.hanover.edu/isle2/index.html?ch=Chapter12

## Lab set A: Word recognition and lexical access

### Lexical Decision Task
- PsyToolkit LDT overview page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/ldt.html
- PsyToolkit LDT run page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_ldt.html
- Hanover Lexical Decision (HTML5/JS): https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/lexicalDecision.html

## Lab set B: Sentence processing with reaction-time output

### Self-paced reading tasks
- PsyToolkit self-paced reading 1 overview: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/pacedreading1.html
- PsyToolkit self-paced reading 1 run page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_pacedreading1.html

- PsyToolkit self-paced reading 2 overview: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/pacedreading2.html
- PsyToolkit self-paced reading 2 run page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_pacedreading2.html

- PsyToolkit self-paced reading 3 overview: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/pacedreading3.html
- PsyToolkit self-paced reading 3 run page: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_pacedreading3.html

## Lab set C: Speech perception and phoneme categories

### Coarticulation, voicing, audiovisual speech, and top-down restoration
- ISLE 12.1 Coarticulation: https://isle.hanover.edu/Ch12Speech/Ch12Coarticulation.html
- ISLE 12.2 Voicing Onset Time: https://isle.hanover.edu/isle2/Ch12Speech/Ch12VOT.html
- ISLE 12.3 McGurk Effect: https://isle.hanover.edu/Ch12Speech/Ch12McGurk.html
- ISLE 12.4 Familiar vs Unfamiliar Languages: https://isle.hanover.edu/Ch12Speech/Ch12Languages.html
- ISLE 12.5 Phonemic Restoration Effect: https://isle.hanover.edu/Ch12Speech/Ch12PhonemeRest.html

## Lab set D: Phonetics and articulation mapping labs

### Interactive articulation and sound mapping
- Sounds of Speech (University of Iowa): https://soundsofspeech.uiowa.edu/
- Seeing Speech IPA charts (click symbols to hear and see articulators): https://www.seeingspeech.ac.uk/ipa-charts/
- Interactive IPA chart (click-to-hear reference): https://www.ipachart.com/

## Teaching ideas and lab designs

### A minimal-prep 50-minute class that feels like a real lab
- Run Lexical Decision first and collect two numbers from each student, such as mean RT for words and mean RT for nonwords
- Run one self-paced reading task using two sentence sets, such as simple syntax versus garden-path style, and collect a single reading-time metric
- Run one ISLE speech perception activity, such as Voicing Onset Time or Phonemic Restoration, and collect a structured judgment, such as where perception flips or how comprehension changes

### Easy variables that students can actually reason about
- You can treat word status as an independent variable in LDT, such as word versus nonword
- You can treat sentence type as an independent variable in self-paced reading, such as straightforward versus syntactically tricky sentences
- You can treat signal quality as an independent variable in Phonemic Restoration by adjusting how much audio is blocked

### Debrief prompts that force “theoretical perspectives” thinking
- Ask what top-down knowledge the brain is using and how you can tell
- Ask what part of the task is language-specific versus general attention and decision making
- Ask what would change if the same task were run in a second language or with unfamiliar vocabulary

### Low-friction data workflow that scales
- Have students submit one difference score per task, such as RT nonword minus RT word, and one sentence condition minus the other
- Plot class distributions later in the Statistics unit to show skew, outliers, and measurement noise
- Re-run one task at the end of the term as a replication exercise and compare distributions
```

### Block 41 (lang=markdown | source=md | block 41)

```markdown
---
title: "PSY-132 Interactive Teaching Labs (Free Only): Life Span Development"
course: "PSY-132 Introductory Psychology"
type: "resource_links"
scope: "teaching_interactive_labs_only_free"
topics:
  - topic_number: 15
    topic_name: "Life Span Development"
created: 2025-12-31
---

## Selection rationale
- These activities are free and student-facing
- These activities behave like labs because students produce outputs you can treat as data, such as quiz scores, classifications, task performance, or structured observations
- These activities support intro-psych debriefs about measurement, development as change over time, and person-by-context effects

## Core interactive lab set

### Prenatal development lab (timeline plus embedded quizzes)
- Endowment for Human Development: Interactive Prenatal Timeline (choose systems, levels, quizzes): https://www.ehd.org/interactive-timeline
- Prenatal Timeline tool (customizable timeline interface): https://www.ehd.org/timeline.php

### Developmental milestones lab (normative development by age, structured checklist output)
- CDC Milestone Tracker app overview (iOS/Android): https://www.cdc.gov/act-early/milestones-app/index.html
- CDC milestones page (includes Digital Online Checklist by age): https://www.cdc.gov/act-early/milestones/index.html

### Cognitive development lab (Piaget-style challenges as playable tasks)
- Piaget’s Cognitive Stages interactive game (multiple challenges by stage): https://www.earlyyears.tv/piagets-cognitive-stages-game/

### Social cognition lab (Theory of Mind and false belief, with feedback)
- OpenLearn Activity: Try the Sally–Anne false belief task (animation plus questions and feedback): https://www.open.edu/openlearn/mod/oucontent/view.php?id=67018&section=1.3

### Attachment across the life span lab (measurable constructs, immediate scoring)
- PsyToolkit Survey Library (choose scales, run demos): https://www.psytoolkit.org/survey-library/
- PsyToolkit State Adult Attachment Measure (SAAM): https://www.psytoolkit.org/survey-library/attachment-saam.html
- OpenLearn free course hub for attachment in early childhood (use as context for interpretation): https://www.open.edu/openlearn/education-development/early-years/attachment-the-early-years/content-section-0

### Adolescence risk-taking lab (behavioral task output, good for development and self-regulation discussion)
- PsyToolkit Balloon Analogue Risk Task (BART) overview page with demo link and data output description: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/bart.html

### Aging and sensory change lab (simulators that produce vivid, debriefable experiences)
- MyEyeDr Vision Simulator (sliders, prompts, keyboard navigation): https://www.myeyedr.com/eye-health/vision-simulator
- eChalk “How old is your hearing?” (interactive frequency test, output age): https://www.echalk.co.uk/Science/biology/hearing/HowOldIsYourHearing/resource.html
- Minnesota DHS Vision and Hearing Loss Simulator landing page (choose context, choose vision loss, choose hearing loss): https://mn.gov/deaf-hard-of-hearing/learning-center/trainings/online.jsp?id=1121-408755
- Direct simulator link: https://pathlore.dhs.mn.gov/Courseware/DisabilityServices/HRDHHS18/simulator/index.html

### Optional lab add-on: age stereotypes and ageism (reaction-time measure)
- Project Implicit test selection (choose an Age IAT when available): https://implicit.harvard.edu/implicit/takeatest.html

## Teaching ideas that keep this “lab-like”

### A clean 50-minute station rotation
- Station 1: Prenatal Timeline and quiz, then record one developmental milestone by week and one quiz score
- Station 2: Milestone checklist for a target age, then record how many milestones were recognized and one surprise item
- Station 3: Sally–Anne false belief task, then record accuracy on each question and what feedback said
- Station 4: Aging simulation, then record one functional barrier the simulation made obvious and one accommodation idea
- Optional Station 5: BART or SAAM, then record one numeric output, such as pumps, explosions, or subscale scores

### Low-friction data capture
- Require one number plus one sentence per station
- Use anonymous codes if you plan to show class distributions

### Debrief prompts that force scientific thinking
- What is the dependent variable in this activity, and how was it measured
- What would threaten validity here, such as device differences, prior knowledge, or demand characteristics
- What would you change to make the activity better approximate a real developmental study
- How does this activity distinguish normative development from individual differences
```

### Block 42 (lang=markdown | source=md | block 42)

```markdown
---
title: "PSY-132 Interactive Teaching Labs (Free Only): Health"
course: "PSY-132 Introductory Psychology"
type: "resource_links"
scope: "teaching_interactive_labs_only_free"
topics:
  - topic_number: 16
    topic_name: "Health"
created: 2025-12-31
---

## Selection rationale
- These activities are free for students to run
- These activities behave like labs because students make choices, manipulate variables, and produce outputs such as graphs, scores, or decisions
- These activities support intro-psych debriefs about health behavior, stress physiology, and how environments shape risk

## Instructor framing that keeps this academically clean
- Treat outputs as demonstrations, not as medical advice or diagnosis
- Use fictional or provided scenarios when an activity could drift into personal disclosure
- Collect only minimal data for grading, such as a screenshot of a graph and one numeric result

## Lab set A: Disease spread and public health decision-making (highly lab-like)

### Model disease spread by manipulating parameters and reading SIR graphs
- HHMI BioInteractive: Modeling Disease Spread (SIR model interactive): https://www.biointeractive.org/classroom-resources/modeling-disease-spread
- Student worksheet (structured prompts and graph interpretation): https://www.biointeractive.org/sites/default/files/media/file/2023-04/ModelingDiseaseSpread-StudentWS-CL.pdf
- Educator materials (implementation guidance and extensions): https://www.biointeractive.org/sites/default/files/media/file/2024-01/ModelingDiseaseSpread-Educator-CL.pdf

### Modify vaccination rate and interpret herd immunity outcomes
- HHMI BioInteractive: Modeling Vaccination Impact on a Measles Epidemic (parameter changes and predictions): https://www.biointeractive.org/classroom-resources/modeling-vaccination-impact-measles-epidemic

### Make outbreak decisions and interpret case data like a disease detective
- CDC Solve the Outbreak (web version): https://www.cdc.gov/digital-social-media-tools/mobile/applications/sto/sto-web.html
- CDC Solve the Outbreak (accessible web version): https://www.cdc.gov/digital-social-media-tools/mobile/applications/sto/508STO.html

## Lab set B: Stress physiology and stress measurement (lab outputs plus debrief)

### Interactive stress feature (short-term vs long-term stress, body responses, coping choices)
- CDC BAM archived teacher hub for the interactive stress feature: https://archive.cdc.gov/www_cdc_gov/healthyschools/bam/teachers/stress-test.html

### Class data collection activity with built-in graphing prompt (students generate a class dataset)
- CDC BAM teacher activity page: The Body-Mind Connection of Stress: https://archive.cdc.gov/www_cdc_gov/healthyschools/bam/teachers/stress-bam.html
- Activity PDF (inventory and graph-the-class-results instructions): https://archive.cdc.gov/www_cdc_gov/healthyschools/bam/teachers/documents/stress_body_mind.pdf

## Lab set C: Health behavior decision labs (nutrition and consumer choice)

### Nutrition Facts label lab games (students practice label-based decisions under time pressure)
- FDA Whyville Snack Shack Games (Label Lingo and Snack Sort): https://www.fda.gov/food/nutrition-education-resources-materials/whyville-snack-shack-games
- Whyville Snack Shack entry (play the games in Whyville): https://www.whyville.net/smmk/top/gates/flax

## Lab set D: Substance use and reward system mechanisms (interactive neurobiology)

### Drag-and-drop synapse lab that links drug effects to reinforcement and health outcomes
- Learn.Genetics Utah: Mouse Party: https://learn.genetics.utah.edu/content/addiction/mouse/
- Mouse Party worksheet (assignable handout): https://teach.genetics.utah.edu/content/addiction/pdfs/Mouse-Party-Worksheet.pdf
- Learn.Genetics Utah: Meth Mouse: https://learn.genetics.utah.edu/content/addiction/methmouse/

## Teaching ideas that keep this unit feeling like an actual lab

### A clean 50-minute class plan that produces class data
- Start with Modeling Disease Spread and require one screenshot of an SIR graph plus one parameter set
- Run Solve the Outbreak for 10–15 minutes and require one decision point plus the reasoning for that decision
- End with a two-question synthesis that links behavior, incentives, and risk perception to outcomes

### A station rotation that feels like “health psych meets public health”
- Station 1: Modeling Disease Spread with one parameter change and one graph interpretation
- Station 2: Measles vaccination modeling with one predicted threshold for “control”
- Station 3: Solve the Outbreak with one key data clue and one decision justification
- Station 4: Stress Body-Mind inventory with one class graph variable and one interpretation sentence
- Station 5: Mouse Party with one drug mechanism and one predicted behavioral effect

### Low-friction grading inputs that scale
- Require one numeric output per station, such as peak infected, time-to-peak, vaccination rate, score, or number of symptoms endorsed
- Require one short explanation per station that labels an independent variable and a dependent variable

### Debrief prompts that force scientific thinking
- What variable did you manipulate, and what outcome changed
- What assumptions are built into the model or game mechanics
- What confounds exist, including device differences, prior knowledge, or time pressure
- What would you measure differently if you were designing a real study on health behavior
```
