```json
        "design_id": "HIST-DESIGN-03",
        "design_name": "Asynchronous lab (learning management system friendly)",
        "steps": [
          "Students complete exactly one exhibit-based lab (Akron or Smithsonian)",
          "Students submit one source card and one paragraph explaining how the artifact reflects a historical assumption in psychology"
        ],
        "grading_artifact": ["One source card", "One paragraph explanation", "One limitation statement"]
      }
    ],
    "debrief_prompts": [
      "What changed over time that can function as an independent variable (methods, institutions, technology, social context)",
      "What counts as evidence in this era, and what could function as the dependent variable (what was measured, what was published, what was funded)",
      "What is one alternative explanation for the shift you identified",
      "What is one ethical hazard if a tool or theory is misapplied",
      "What is one thing you cannot infer from this artifact or timeline entry"
    ]
  }
}
```

### Block 55 (lang=markdown | source=md | block 55)

```markdown
---
title: "PSY-132 Interactive Teaching Labs: Theoretical Perspectives"
filename: "psy-132-topic-2-theoretical-perspectives-interactive-teaching-labs-free"
type: "resource_links"
status: "curated"
created: "2026-01-11"
updated: "2026-01-11"
origin: "Curated for PSY-132 Topic 2 with strict emphasis on free, student-facing interactive teaching labs that let students experience a perspective and then map its assumptions"
citation_style: "none"
verification_needed: false
tags:
  - "psy-132"
  - "theoretical-perspectives"
  - "interactive-labs"
  - "free"
topics:
  - "Theoretical Perspectives"
aliases: []
sources:
  - "https://phet.colorado.edu/sims/html/neuron/latest/neuron_en.html"
  - "https://educationalgames.nobelprize.org/educational/medicine/pavlov/pavlov.html"
  - "https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_stroop.html"
  - "https://implicit.harvard.edu/implicit/takeatest.html"
  - "https://ncase.me/trust/"
  - "https://www.gapminder.org/fw/world-health-chart/"
  - "https://www.valuescardsort.com/"
  - "https://www.learner.org/series/discovering-psychology/explorations/approaches-in-practice/"
cssclasses: []
notes: "This topic is best taught as a set of short labs where each activity embodies one perspective. Grade classification and reasoning, not personal results."
---

## Selection rationale
- Perspectives are conceptual lenses, so the most teachable “lab” format is repeated exposure to mini-activities that produce an output and then require perspective mapping
- Each activity below produces a recordable output: a score, a reaction-time effect, a decision pattern, a plotted trend, or a saved values profile
- All links are free and student-facing

## Interactive teaching labs

## Lab: Biological perspective (mechanisms, brain, neurons)
- Link
  - https://phet.colorado.edu/sims/html/neuron/latest/neuron_en.html
- Activity type
  - Simulation with manipulable variables
- Output type
  - Screenshot of a firing pattern plus parameter settings
- Typical completion time
  - 10–15 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - One screenshot
  - One variable-change note: “I changed X and saw Y”
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require a mechanism statement: “The biological perspective explains behavior via neural processes”

## Lab: Behavioral perspective (learning via conditioning)
- Link
  - https://educationalgames.nobelprize.org/educational/medicine/pavlov/pavlov.html
- Activity type
  - Interactive conditioning game
- Output type
  - Trial outcome pattern and a brief contingency description
- Typical completion time
  - 10–15 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - Screenshot of outcome
  - One sentence identifying CS, US, CR, UR
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require “observable behavior only” phrasing for the behavioral lens

## Lab: Cognitive perspective (information processing limits)
- Link
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_stroop.html
- Activity type
  - Reaction-time task
- Output type
  - Congruent vs incongruent performance difference
- Typical completion time
  - 5–10 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - Screenshot of results
  - One numeric difference score if shown
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require a processing explanation: “Interference occurs because reading is automatic and competes with color naming”

## Lab: Psychodynamic bridge lab (automatic, not fully conscious processing)
- Link
  - https://implicit.harvard.edu/implicit/takeatest.html
- Activity type
  - Timed categorization task with feedback
- Output type
  - Completion evidence plus methods reflection
- Typical completion time
  - 10–20 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - Screenshot of completion screen
  - One methods limitation sentence
- Instructor framing notes
  - Frame this as “automatic cognition” and “nonconscious processes,” not as a clinical or diagnostic interpretation

## Lab: Evolutionary perspective (strategic interaction, cooperation)
- Link
  - https://ncase.me/trust/
- Activity type
  - Interactive simulation of repeated games
- Output type
  - Strategy outcomes and a short explanation of what worked and why
- Typical completion time
  - 15–25 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - One screenshot of an outcome
  - One strategy note: “Strategy A outperformed B when X changed”
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require an adaptation logic statement: “Which strategy survives across repeated interaction and why”

## Lab: Sociocultural perspective (context and systems)
- Link
  - https://www.gapminder.org/fw/world-health-chart/
- Activity type
  - Interactive dataset visualization
- Output type
  - Country comparison pattern over time
- Typical completion time
  - 10–20 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - Screenshot of a comparison
  - One claim with a limitation: “This is group-level data”
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require an ecological fallacy warning and one context hypothesis

## Lab: Humanistic perspective (values, meaning, choice)
- Link
  - https://www.valuescardsort.com/
- Activity type
  - Drag-and-drop values sorting tool
- Output type
  - Saved or captured values profile
- Typical completion time
  - 10–20 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - Screenshot or exported output
  - One sentence explaining why one value rose to the top in the scenario provided
- Instructor framing notes
  - Use a fictional scenario by default so students are not graded on personal disclosure

## Lab: Multi-perspective comparison lab (explicitly contrasts approaches)
- Link
  - https://www.learner.org/series/discovering-psychology/explorations/approaches-in-practice/
- Activity type
  - Interactive exploration comparing approaches
- Output type
  - Completed “approach match” response set
- Typical completion time
  - 15–25 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - Screenshot of one segment
  - One “approach match” table: perspective, key assumption, best-fit evidence
- Instructor framing notes
  - Treat this as the capstone synthesis for Topic 2

## Teaching designs and ideas

## Option: 50-minute station rotation that forces perspective mapping
- Station 1: Pavlov game
- Station 2: Stroop
- Station 3: Neuron sim
- Station 4: Gapminder
- Wrap: Students complete a perspective match table

Grading artifact
- One screenshot per station
- One row per station in a perspective match table

## Option: Hypothesis-first mini-study inside Topic 2
- Pre-specify a question: “Which perspective best explains performance in this task and what would it predict if we changed X”
- Students run Stroop or Neuron
- Students submit:
  - the output
  - the prediction
  - the perspective justification

## Debrief prompts that keep this lab-like
- What is the dependent variable in the activity
- What mechanism does each perspective claim explains the output
- What would a different perspective treat as the key variable
- What is one limitation of interpreting the output through only one lens
---
```

### Block 57 (lang=markdown | source=md | block 57)

```markdown
---
title: "PSY-132 Interactive Teaching Labs: Research Methods"
filename: "psy-132-topic-3-research-methods-interactive-teaching-labs-free"
type: "resource_links"
status: "curated"
created: "2026-01-11"
updated: "2026-01-11"
origin: "Curated for PSY-132 Topic 3 with strict emphasis on free, student-facing interactive teaching labs that produce debriefable outputs (choices, reaction time, accuracy, graphs, CSV exports, or structured research plans)"
citation_style: "none"
verification_needed: false
tags:
  - "psy-132"
  - "research-methods"
  - "interactive-labs"
  - "free"
topics:
  - "Research Methods"
aliases: []
sources:
  - "https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/"
  - "https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_stroop.html"
  - "https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_flanker.html"
  - "https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_digitspan.html"
  - "https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/cognition.html"
  - "https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/mentRot.html"
  - "https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/stroop.html"
  - "https://iscience.uni-konstanz.de/archive/ulf/Lab/WebExpPsyLab.html"
  - "https://undsci.berkeley.edu/for-educators/find-lessons-and-tools/how-science-works-interactive/"
  - "https://lab.js.org/"
  - "https://labjs.felixhenninger.com/"
  - "https://www.jspsych.org/"
  - "https://github.com/jspsych/experiment-demos"
cssclasses: []
notes: "This topic is about method decisions, not content coverage. Grade the method work products (IV, DV, operational definitions, confounds, validity limits, and conclusions). Avoid grading personal performance."
---

## Selection rationale
- Research methods is easiest to teach by running small experiments and then forcing students to name the variables and validity threats
- Each activity below produces recordable outputs suitable for online-lab grading at scale
- All links are free and student-facing in a browser

## Core lab hubs you can reuse all semester

### Hub 1: Run classic experiments quickly
- PsyToolkit Experiment Library
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/

### Hub 2: Parameter manipulation and CSV export
- Hanover Cognition Laboratory Experiments (HTML5/JS hub)
  - https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/cognition.html

### Hub 3: Participate in real web experiments
- Web Experimental Psychology Lab (Konstanz archive hub)
  - https://iscience.uni-konstanz.de/archive/ulf/Lab/WebExpPsyLab.html

### Hub 4: Build a simple experiment
- lab.js (overview)
  - https://lab.js.org/
- lab.js Builder (web app)
  - https://labjs.felixhenninger.com/
- jsPsych (overview)
  - https://www.jspsych.org/
- jsPsych experiment demos (GitHub)
  - https://github.com/jspsych/experiment-demos

## Interactive teaching labs

## Lab 1: Run a reaction-time experiment and extract IV and DV
- PsyToolkit Stroop (run page)
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_stroop.html
- PsyToolkit Flanker (run page)
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_flanker.html

Activity type
- Reaction-time experiment

Output type
- Screenshot of results
- One difference score if displayed
- One methods paragraph identifying IV, DV, and one confound

Typical completion time
- 10–20 minutes

Submission evidence format
- Screenshot
- Numeric output if available
- Short reflection

Instructor framing notes
- Emphasize operational definitions
  - “Interference” is defined as a condition difference in RT or errors
- Emphasize threats to validity in online labs
  - device latency, distractions, practice effects, misunderstanding instructions

## Lab 2: Run a cognitive measure as a measurement and reliability lab
- PsyToolkit Digit Span (run page)
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_digitspan.html

Activity type
- Performance-based measure

Output type
- Maximum span or final score
- One reliability plan for re-testing

Typical completion time
- 5–10 minutes

Submission evidence format
- Screenshot
- Numeric output
- Short reflection

Instructor framing notes
- Force the distinction between measurement and construct
  - span score is a proxy for a construct, not the construct itself
- Require a test–retest plan
  - when to retest and what you expect to change or remain stable

## Lab 3: Parameter manipulation and data export lab
- Hanover Mental Rotation (HTML5/JS)
  - https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/mentRot.html
- Hanover Stroop (HTML5/JS)
  - https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/stroop.html

Activity type
- Experiment with adjustable parameters and downloadable data

Output type
- Screenshot of parameter settings
- Screenshot of results
- CSV export if feasible for your class workflow

Typical completion time
- 15–25 minutes

Submission evidence format
- Screenshot
- Numeric output
- Optional CSV file upload

Instructor framing notes
- Assign one parameter to manipulate
  - number of trials, timing, difficulty, stimulus set
- Require a prediction before the run and an interpretation after the run

## Lab 4: Subject pool and sampling lab
- Web Experimental Psychology Lab hub
  - https://iscience.uni-konstanz.de/archive/ulf/Lab/WebExpPsyLab.html

Activity type
- Participate in a web experiment and critique the method

Output type
- Brief “methods audit card”
  - what was the task
  - what was measured
  - what kind of sampling is implied
  - what bias might exist

Typical completion time
- 15–30 minutes

Submission evidence format
- Screenshot or completion evidence
- Short reflection

Instructor framing notes
- This is a recruitment and sampling lesson
  - who ends up in online studies and who does not

## Lab 5: Science workflow documentation lab
- UC Berkeley Understanding Science: How Science Works Interactive
  - https://undsci.berkeley.edu/for-educators/find-lessons-and-tools/how-science-works-interactive/

Activity type
- Interactive research-process planning tool

Output type
- Completed workflow artifact
  - research question, hypothesis, variables, design choice, evidence plan, alternative explanations

Typical completion time
- 15–25 minutes

Submission evidence format
- Screenshot or exported artifact
- Short reflection

Instructor framing notes
- Require at least one rival hypothesis and one boundary condition

## Lab 6: Build-your-own micro-experiment lab
- lab.js Builder
  - https://labjs.felixhenninger.com/
- jsPsych demos
  - https://github.com/jspsych/experiment-demos

Activity type
- Create or modify a simple experiment

Output type
- One runnable task design plus a written method section

Typical completion time
- 30–60 minutes
  - best as a dedicated lab day or take-home lab

Submission evidence format
- Screenshot of the build
- Link or exported file if you use a submission channel for files
- Short method section

Instructor framing notes
- Keep scope minimal
  - 10–20 trials
  - one IV with 2 levels
  - one DV
- Grade the method section, not the code aesthetics

## Teaching designs and ideas

## Option A: 50-minute “IV and DV bootcamp” lab day
- Run Stroop or Flanker
- Students submit:
  - IV statement
  - DV statement
  - one operational definition
  - one confound and one fix

Grading artifact
- One screenshot
- Four-item method response set

## Option B: Station rotation that produces a class dataset
- Station 1: PsyToolkit Stroop
- Station 2: PsyToolkit Digit Span
- Station 3: Hanover Mental Rotation with one parameter change
- Station 4: Understanding Science workflow artifact

Grading artifact
- One number per station plus one limitation per station

## Option C: Mini-study proposal inside Intro Psych constraints
- Provide a menu of feasible IVs
  - time pressure, distraction, stimulus complexity, practice
- Students choose one and write:
  - hypothesis
  - design type
  - operational definitions
  - planned analysis in plain language
  - one validity threat and mitigation

## Debrief prompts that keep this lab-like
- What is the independent variable and what are its levels
- What is the dependent variable and how is it quantified
- What is one alternative explanation that does not require your preferred theory
- What is one confound unique to online experiments and how would you mitigate it
- What conclusion is justified and what conclusion would be overreach
---
```

### Block 59 (lang=markdown | source=md | block 59)

```markdown
---
title: "PSY-132 Interactive Teaching Labs: Statistics"
filename: "psy-132-topic-4-statistics-interactive-teaching-labs-free"
type: "resource_links"
status: "curated"
created: "2026-01-11"
updated: "2026-01-11"
origin: "Curated for PSY-132 Topic 4 with strict emphasis on free, student-facing interactive teaching labs that produce debriefable outputs (graphs, sampling distributions, confidence intervals, randomization results, and data visualizations)"
citation_style: "none"
verification_needed: false
tags:
  - "psy-132"
  - "statistics"
  - "interactive-labs"
  - "free"
topics:
  - "Statistics"
aliases: []
sources:
  - "https://www.lock5stat.com/StatKey/"
  - "https://onlinestatbook.com/stat_sim/"
  - "https://www.rossmanchance.com/applets.html"
  - "https://codap.concord.org/"
  - "https://tuvalabs.com/tools/"
  - "https://www.gapminder.org/fw/world-health-chart/"
  - "https://seeing-theory.brown.edu/"
cssclasses: []
notes: "This topic should feel like a lab course. Students manipulate data or parameters, observe distributions and intervals, and then write claims with appropriate uncertainty. Grade graphs and interpretation, not math fluency alone."
---

## Selection rationale
- Statistics is best learned by simulation and interactive visualization rather than formula-first instruction
- Each activity produces a recordable output suitable for grading at scale
  - screenshot of a graph or distribution
  - one numeric result such as a confidence interval bound
  - one plain-language interpretation with a limitation
- All links are free and student-facing

## Interactive teaching labs

## Lab: Bootstrap confidence intervals (intervals as simulated distributions)
- Link
  - https://www.lock5stat.com/StatKey/
  - https://www.lock5stat.com/StatKey/bootstrap_1_quant/bootstrap_1_quant.html
- Activity type
  - Bootstrap simulation with editable or uploadable data
- Output type
  - bootstrap distribution plot
  - confidence interval bounds
- Typical completion time
  - 15–25 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot of the bootstrap distribution
  - two numbers for the interval endpoints
  - one interpretation sentence in plain language
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require students to identify the statistic being bootstrapped
  - Require a claim that matches the interval, not a stronger claim

## Lab: Randomization test for a difference (inference without normality assumptions)
- Link
  - https://www.lock5stat.com/StatKey/randomization_1_quant_1_cat/randomization_1_quant_1_cat.html
- Activity type
  - randomization simulation with shuffle-based null distribution
- Output type
  - null distribution plot
  - p-value estimate or tail proportion
- Typical completion time
  - 15–25 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot of the null distribution with the observed statistic marked
  - one p-value or tail proportion
  - one conclusion sentence that uses correct uncertainty language
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require students to state the null hypothesis in words
  - Require students to define the comparison groups clearly

## Lab: Sampling distributions and the Central Limit Theorem (repeated sampling)
- Link
  - https://onlinestatbook.com/stat_sim/sampling_dist/
  - https://onlinestatbook.com/stat_sim/samp_dist_js/index.html
- Activity type
  - interactive simulation generating sampling distributions
- Output type
  - sampling distribution plots under different sample sizes
- Typical completion time
  - 15–25 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - two screenshots showing different sample sizes
  - one sentence describing what changed and what did not change
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require a clear distinction between population distribution and sampling distribution
  - Require a prediction before running the second condition

## Lab: Correlation intuition and outliers (what correlation “feels like”)
- Link
  - https://www.rossmanchance.com/applets/GuessCorrelation.html
- Activity type
  - interactive estimation task with immediate feedback
- Output type
  - estimated correlation values and feedback
  - qualitative notes on outliers and nonlinearity
- Typical completion time
  - 10–20 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot of one example with feedback
  - one short explanation of how outliers or nonlinear patterns affect correlation
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require a correlation versus causation warning
  - Require a “what would improve this analysis” note, such as plotting first or checking nonlinearity

## Lab: Exploratory data analysis with drag-and-drop visualization (EDA as workflow)
- Link
  - https://codap.concord.org/
  - https://codap.concord.org/get-started/
- Activity type
  - interactive data analysis environment
- Output type
  - student-built plots and summary statistics
- Typical completion time
  - 20–40 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot of one plot and one summary statistic output
  - one claim written as a descriptive statement, not an inference claim
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require students to label variables and units
  - Require one data-quality note, such as missingness, outliers, or measurement ambiguity

## Lab: Guided statistics practice with authentic datasets (interactive tasks)
- Link
  - https://tuvalabs.com/tools/
  - https://tuvalabs.com/tutorials/
- Activity type
  - interactive tutorials and dataset-driven tasks
- Output type
  - completed tutorial outputs and graphs
- Typical completion time
  - 20–40 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot of completed graph or task output
  - one short interpretation sentence
- Instructor framing notes
  - Assign one tutorial so students share a common dataset for debrief
  - Require a limitation statement about representativeness or measurement

## Lab: Real-world trend exploration (data over time, comparisons, and confounds)
- Link
  - https://www.gapminder.org/fw/world-health-chart/
- Activity type
  - interactive time-series visualization with country comparisons
- Output type
  - time-playable scatterplot trend patterns
- Typical completion time
  - 10–25 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot showing two countries over time
  - one claim and one confound
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require group-level language and ecological fallacy avoidance
  - Require a concrete confound hypothesis such as policy, war, disease burden, or measurement change

## Optional concept-lab visuals (use as pre-lab or debrief visuals)
- Link
  - https://seeing-theory.brown.edu/
- Activity type
  - interactive concept visualizations
- Output type
  - screenshots plus concept explanations
- Typical completion time
  - 10–20 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot plus one “what this shows” sentence
- Instructor framing notes
  - Use to preview or consolidate concepts, not as the only lab experience

## Teaching designs and ideas

## Option: 50-minute lab day focused on inference
- Part 1: Sampling distributions simulation
- Part 2: Bootstrap interval in StatKey
- Part 3: One interpretation paragraph with correct uncertainty language

Grading artifact
- Two screenshots
- One interval
- One interpretation paragraph

## Option: Station rotation for mixed skill levels
- Station 1: Guess the Correlation
- Station 2: Sampling distributions simulation
- Station 3: StatKey bootstrap interval
- Station 4: CODAP quick plot with a provided dataset

Grading artifact
- One screenshot per station
- One sentence per station identifying what the output represents

## Option: Asynchronous online lab that produces a reusable class dataset
- Students run one StatKey activity and submit one numeric result plus a screenshot
- Instructor aggregates results and uses them later for:
  - distribution shape
  - outliers
  - interval interpretation
  - difference between individual result and class-level pattern

## Debrief prompts that keep this lab-like
- What is the statistic and what is being treated as the sample
- What is the output and what does it represent, such as sampling distribution, null distribution, or bootstrap distribution
- What claim is justified and what claim would be overreach
- What would change if the sample were larger or if the measurement were noisier
- What confound or bias could distort your interpretation
---
```

```json
        "submission_evidence_format": ["screenshot", "short_reflection"],
        "submission_requirements": [
          "Two screenshots showing different sample sizes",
          "One sentence describing what changed and what did not change"
        ],
        "instructor_framing_notes": [
          "Require distinction between population distribution and sampling distribution",
          "Require a prediction before running the second condition"
        ],
        "privacy_and_safety_notes": "Low risk. No personal disclosure required.",
        "opt_out_available": false
      },
      {
        "lab_title": "Correlation intuition and outliers (what correlation feels like)",
        "urls": ["https://www.rossmanchance.com/applets/GuessCorrelation.html"],
        "activity_type": "interactive_estimation_task",
        "output_types": ["numeric_output", "graph_or_model_output"],
        "typical_completion_time_minutes": { "min": 10, "max": 20 },
        "submission_evidence_format": ["screenshot", "short_reflection"],
        "submission_requirements": [
          "Screenshot of one example with feedback",
          "One short explanation of how outliers or nonlinear patterns affect correlation"
        ],
        "instructor_framing_notes": [
          "Require a correlation versus causation warning",
          "Require one improvement note such as plotting first or checking nonlinearity"
        ],
        "privacy_and_safety_notes": "Low risk. No personal disclosure required.",
        "opt_out_available": false
      },
      {

        ],

    "debrief_prompts": [

      "What confound or bias could distort interpretation"
```

### Block 61 (lang=markdown | source=md | block 61)

```markdown
---
title: "PSY-132 Interactive Teaching Labs: Ethics"
filename: "psy-132-topic-5-ethics-interactive-teaching-labs-free"
type: "resource_links"
status: "curated"
created: "2026-01-11"
updated: "2026-01-11"
origin: "Curated for PSY-132 Topic 5 with strict emphasis on free, student-facing interactive teaching labs focused on research ethics, human subjects protections, and ethical decision-making"
citation_style: "none"
verification_needed: true
tags:
  - "psy-132"
  - "ethics"
  - "interactive-labs"
  - "free"
topics:
  - "Ethics"
aliases: []
sources:
  - "https://ori.hhs.gov/the-lab"
  - "https://ori.hhs.gov/research-clinic"
  - "https://www.hhs.gov/ohrp/education-and-outreach/human-research-protection-training/participant-centered-informed-consent-training/index.html"
  - "https://www.open.edu/openlearn/society-politics-law/why-do-we-need-research-ethics"
  - "https://moralmachine.mit.edu/"
  - "https://improvinghealthcare.mehp.upenn.edu/course/ethics-research-human-subjects"
  - "https://quandarygame.org/play"
cssclasses: []
notes: "Ethics labs should be graded on methods reasoning, not moral agreement. Default to vignette-based responses and provide an opt-out alternative. Click-test links before release."
---

## Selection rationale
- Ethics is most teachable through decision points and consequence tracing rather than lecture-only coverage
- Each activity below produces recordable outputs suitable for grading at scale
  - decision path and outcome
  - completion evidence and a methods reflection
  - scored quiz results where available
- All links are free and student-facing

## Interactive teaching labs

## Lab: Research integrity and misconduct (decision-based simulation)
- Link
  - https://ori.hhs.gov/the-lab
- Activity type
  - Interactive movie with decision points
- Output type
  - Decision path plus outcome screen
- Typical completion time
  - 20–45 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - Screenshot of completion or final outcome
  - Short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Treat this as a process lab about incentives, pressures, and questionable research practices
  - Require students to name one prevention control, such as data management plan, supervision practice, authorship agreement

## Lab: Research integrity clinical reasoning (shorter ORI scenario format)
- Link
  - https://ori.hhs.gov/research-clinic
- Activity type
  - Interactive training scenario
- Output type
  - Chosen actions and consequences
- Typical completion time
  - 15–30 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - Screenshot of completion evidence
  - Short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require a distinction between ethical lapse, questionable research practice, and misconduct
  - Require one “what would you do differently earlier” prevention statement

## Lab: Informed consent as a decision workflow (human subjects protections)
- Link
  - https://www.hhs.gov/ohrp/education-and-outreach/human-research-protection-training/participant-centered-informed-consent-training/index.html
- Activity type
  - Interactive training modules
- Output type
  - Completion evidence plus a consent-quality critique
- Typical completion time
  - 20–40 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - Screenshot of module completion
  - Short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require students to list the minimum components of consent in plain language
  - Require one vulnerability or accessibility consideration

## Lab: Ethics committee role-play challenge (research ethics decisions)
- Link
  - https://www.open.edu/openlearn/society-politics-law/why-do-we-need-research-ethics
- Activity type
  - Interactive challenge framed as committee decisions
- Output type
  - Case decision plus justification
- Typical completion time
  - 15–30 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - Screenshot of the decision or end screen
  - Short justification paragraph
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require students to identify risks, benefits, and one mitigation
  - Require a statement about what additional information they would need before approving

## Lab: Ethical dilemmas and tradeoffs (consequence-based choices)
- Link
  - https://moralmachine.mit.edu/
- Activity type
  - Interactive dilemma choices with aggregated comparison
- Output type
  - Decision record plus a principles explanation
- Typical completion time
  - 10–20 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - Screenshot of a completed scenario set or results view
  - Short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Do not grade on choice direction
  - Require students to name the principle they were prioritizing, such as minimizing harm, fairness, duty, rights

## Lab: Ethics knowledge checks with quizzes (structured assessment)
- Link
  - https://improvinghealthcare.mehp.upenn.edu/course/ethics-research-human-subjects
- Activity type
  - Interactive module with quizzes
- Output type
  - Quiz completion evidence plus one methods takeaway
- Typical completion time
  - 20–45 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - Screenshot of quiz completion
  - Short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require one takeaway stated as an action rule a researcher would follow
  - Require one example of a boundary case where the rule is ambiguous

## Optional lab: General ethical decision-making game (applied reasoning practice)
- Link
  - https://quandarygame.org/play
- Activity type
  - Interactive ethics decision game
- Output type
  - Decision path and outcomes
- Typical completion time
  - 15–30 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - Screenshot of completion or results
  - Short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Use as a transfer task after research ethics content
  - Require students to map their reasoning to one ethical framework, such as consequentialism, deontology, virtue ethics

## Safety and privacy defaults for this topic
- Grade completion and reasoning, not moral agreement
- Allow an opt-out option for any activity that feels personally activating
  - Provide an instructor screenshot set and have students analyze the decisions and consequences instead
- Avoid requiring students to disclose personal experiences with trauma, mental health, or illegal behavior

## Teaching designs and ideas

## Option: 50-minute lab day, research ethics focus
- Part 1: ORI scenario work in small groups
- Part 2: Informed consent critique using OHRP module
- Part 3: Submit a one-page ethics audit
  - risk, benefit, mitigation, consent, data integrity, authorship

## Option: Station rotation for mixed pacing
- Station 1: ORI The Lab
- Station 2: OpenLearn ethics challenge
- Station 3: Moral Machine
- Station 4: Consent critique mini-task

Grading artifact
- One screenshot per station
- One paragraph total that includes one IV, one DV, and one validity or ethics threat applied to research

## Option: Asynchronous online lab with standardized prompts
- Students complete one interactive activity
- Students submit:
  - screenshot
  - three short answers
    - what was the key decision
    - what principle or rule guided the decision
    - what information would you require before approving the study or action

## Debrief prompts that keep this lab-like
- What was the decision point and what were the available options
- What foreseeable consequences followed each option
- What ethical principle or rule did you prioritize and why
- What information was missing that would change the decision
- What mitigation would reduce harm while preserving the research question
---
```

### Block 63 (lang=markdown | source=md | block 63)

```markdown
---
title: "PSY-132 Interactive Teaching Labs: Neuroscience"
filename: "psy-132-topic-6-neuroscience-interactive-teaching-labs-free"
type: "resource_links"
status: "curated"
created: "2026-01-11"
updated: "2026-01-11"
origin: "Curated for PSY-132 Topic 6 with strict emphasis on free, student-facing interactive teaching labs that produce debriefable outputs (parameter changes, labeled structures, graphs, screenshots, and short evidence claims)"
citation_style: "none"
verification_needed: true
tags:
  - "psy-132"
  - "neuroscience"
  - "interactive-labs"
  - "free"
topics:
  - "Neuroscience"
aliases: []
sources:
  - "https://phet.colorado.edu/en/simulations/neuron"
  - "https://phet.colorado.edu/sims/html/neuron/latest/neuron_en.html"
  - "https://phet.colorado.edu/en/simulation/membrane-channels"
  - "https://www.biointeractive.org/classroom-resources/electrical-activity-neurons"
  - "https://www.biointeractive.org/classroom-resources/neurophysiology-virtual-lab"
  - "https://www.brainfacts.org/3d-brain"
  - "https://neurotorium.org/tool/brain-atlas/"
  - "https://atlas.brain-map.org/atlas"
  - "https://sketchfab.com/3d-models/the-nervous-system-2e6be1399756494b9f185ce8c5900911"
  - "https://dnalc.cshl.edu/resources/products/3d-brain-app.html"
cssclasses: []
notes: "Neuroscience labs should be graded on mechanism statements and evidence from the activity outputs, not memorized anatomy lists. Click-test links before release."
---

## Selection rationale
- Neuroscience is most teachable when students manipulate a model, observe a change, and then write a mechanism statement
- The activities below produce recordable outputs suitable for grading at scale
  - screenshots of parameter settings and outcomes
  - labeled structure identifications
  - graph interpretations and causal-chain explanations bounded to the model
- All links are free and student-facing

## Interactive teaching labs

## Lab: Neuron firing and action potentials
- Links
  - https://phet.colorado.edu/en/simulations/neuron
  - https://phet.colorado.edu/sims/html/neuron/latest/neuron_en.html
- Activity type
  - Simulation with manipulable variables
- Output type
  - parameter settings plus an observed outcome change
- Typical completion time
  - 10–20 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require a two-step mechanism statement
    - Manipulation, physiological change, observable output
  - Require one limitation statement
    - This is a simplified model and omits many biological details

## Lab: Membrane channels and ion flow
- Link
  - https://phet.colorado.edu/en/simulation/membrane-channels
- Activity type
  - Build-and-test membrane simulation
- Output type
  - before and after state screenshots plus a claim about why flow changed
- Typical completion time
  - 10–20 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - two screenshots
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require an operational definition of the dependent variable
    - Flow rate, direction of flow, or net charge change as shown in the interface

## Lab: Recording neural activity and interpreting graphs
- Links
  - https://www.biointeractive.org/classroom-resources/electrical-activity-neurons
  - https://www.biointeractive.org/classroom-resources/neurophysiology-virtual-lab
- Activity type
  - Interactive lab modules with embedded questions and data displays
- Output type
  - graph interpretation plus a method note
- Typical completion time
  - 20–40 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require students to label what the graph axes represent and what changed across conditions
  - Require one validity note
    - What the graph can support and what it cannot

## Lab: 3D neuroanatomy scavenger hunt
- Links
  - https://www.brainfacts.org/3d-brain
  - https://neurotorium.org/tool/brain-atlas/
- Activity type
  - Interactive 3D structure identification
- Output type
  - labeled structure selections plus a structure-to-function mapping claim
- Typical completion time
  - 15–25 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - categorical output
- Instructor framing notes
  - Provide a target list of 6–10 structures
  - Require each structure to be paired with one cautious function statement
    - Avoid absolute phrasing and avoid clinical claims

## Lab: Brain atlas navigation and hierarchical labeling
- Link
  - https://atlas.brain-map.org/atlas
- Activity type
  - Interactive atlas exploration
- Output type
  - evidence of navigation plus a short ontology note
- Typical completion time
  - 15–30 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require students to report the path they followed, such as region to subregion to structure
  - Require one sentence explaining why hierarchical labeling matters for scientific communication

## Optional lab: Whole nervous system 3D model exploration
- Link
  - https://sketchfab.com/3d-models/the-nervous-system-2e6be1399756494b9f185ce8c5900911
- Activity type
  - Interactive 3D model exploration
- Output type
  - structure identification and a systems-level pathway claim
- Typical completion time
  - 10–20 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require a pathway description
    - sensory input to CNS processing to motor output
  - Require one limitation
    - Model is anatomical and does not show neural signaling dynamics

## Optional lab: Mobile-based brain structures scavenger hunt
- Link
  - https://dnalc.cshl.edu/resources/products/3d-brain-app.html
- Activity type
  - App-based interactive structure identification
- Output type
  - structure identification list plus a brief function mapping
- Typical completion time
  - 15–25 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - categorical output
- Instructor framing notes
  - Use only if your class can reliably access apps
  - Default alternative
    - BrainFacts 3D Brain

## Teaching designs and ideas

## Option: 50-minute mechanism-first lab day
- Part 1: PhET Neuron with one assigned manipulation
- Part 2: Membrane Channels with a before and after comparison
- Part 3: One short written mechanism chain
  - Variable, physiological change, observed output, one limitation

Grading artifact
- Two screenshots
- One mechanism chain paragraph

## Option: Station rotation for mixed pacing
- Station 1: PhET Neuron
- Station 2: Membrane Channels
- Station 3: BrainFacts 3D Brain scavenger hunt
- Station 4: HHMI neural activity module segment

Grading artifact
- One screenshot per station
- One IV and DV statement per station
- One limitation per station

## Option: Asynchronous online lab that feeds Topic 4 later
- Students run PhET Neuron and record a binary outcome
  - spike occurred or did not occur under a defined setting
- Students submit the setting and outcome
- Instructor aggregates and uses the dataset later for
  - proportions, variability, and design critique

## Debrief prompts that keep this lab-like
- What is the independent variable you manipulated or the condition that differed
- What is the dependent variable and how is it represented in the interface
- What mechanism explains the observed change, based on the model and only the model
- What is one alternative explanation, such as misunderstanding the control or device differences
- What conclusion would be overreach given the simplifications of the model
---
```

### Block 65 (lang=markdown | source=md | block 65)

```markdown
---
title: "PSY-132 Interactive Teaching Labs: Sensation"
filename: "psy-132-topic-7-sensation-interactive-teaching-labs-free"
type: "resource_links"
status: "curated"
created: "2026-01-11"
updated: "2026-01-11"
origin: "Curated for PSY-132 Topic 7 with strict emphasis on free, student-facing interactive teaching labs that produce debriefable outputs (thresholds, JNDs, SDT decisions, ROC shifts, and stimulus parameter effects)"
citation_style: "none"
verification_needed: true
tags:
  - "psy-132"
  - "sensation"
  - "interactive-labs"
  - "free"
topics:
  - "Sensation"
aliases: []
sources:
  - "https://isle.hanover.edu/Chapter02.html"
  - "https://isle.hanover.edu/isle2/index.html?ch=Chapter02"
  - "https://phet.colorado.edu/en/simulations/color-vision"
  - "https://phet.colorado.edu/sims/html/color-vision/latest/color-vision_en.html"
  - "https://phet.colorado.edu/en/simulations/sound-waves"
  - "https://phet.colorado.edu/sims/html/sound-waves/latest/sound-waves_all.html"
  - "https://www.phys.unsw.edu.au/jw/hearing.html"
cssclasses: []
notes: "Sensation labs should emphasize psychophysics and measurement. Grade operational definitions and evidence from outputs (threshold estimates, SDT outcomes, parameter changes), not subjective opinions. Click-test links before release."
---

## Selection rationale
- Sensation is naturally lab-driven because the core questions are measurement questions
- These activities produce recordable outputs suitable for grading at scale
  - thresholds and JND estimates
  - signal detection choices and ROC shifts
  - stimulus parameter manipulations with visible and audible effects
- All links are free and student-facing

## Interactive teaching labs

## Lab: Psychophysics methods hub (thresholds, JND, adjustment, and SDT)
- Links
  - https://isle.hanover.edu/Chapter02.html
  - https://isle.hanover.edu/isle2/index.html?ch=Chapter02
- Activity type
  - Interactive psychophysics labs
- Output type
  - threshold estimate or JND estimate
  - SDT decision outcomes and ROC movement
- Typical completion time
  - 20–40 minutes for a multi-part lab day
  - 10–20 minutes for a single activity
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - numeric output
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Assign a specific method and stimulus so students produce comparable outputs
  - Require an operational definition for the DV
    - threshold as a criterion on responses
    - JND as a difference threshold estimate
  - Require one validity limitation
    - device differences, screen size, headphone quality, background noise, practice effects

Suggested ISLE mini-lab menu for Topic 7
- Method of limits for absolute threshold and difference threshold
- Method of constant stimuli for absolute threshold and difference threshold
- Method of adjustment for threshold estimation
- Signal detection decision shifts and ROC curve movement

## Lab: Signal detection theory lab (decision criteria and ROC)
- Link
  - Use the SDT and ROC activities from the ISLE Chapter 2 hub above
- Activity type
  - SDT decision-making simulation
- Output type
  - hits, misses, false alarms, correct rejections
  - criterion shifts and ROC shifts
- Typical completion time
  - 10–20 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - numeric output
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require a confusion-matrix statement
  - Require a criterion statement in plain language
    - how strict the student set their decision rule

## Lab: Visual sensation lab (color mixing and wavelength)
- Links
  - https://phet.colorado.edu/en/simulations/color-vision
  - https://phet.colorado.edu/sims/html/color-vision/latest/color-vision_en.html
- Activity type
  - Simulation with manipulable stimulus parameters
- Output type
  - parameter settings and perceived color outcomes
- Typical completion time
  - 10–20 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - two screenshots
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require a stimulus-control description
    - which sliders or wavelength settings were changed
  - Require a mechanistic claim at the level of cones and light mixture
  - Require one boundary condition
    - the sim models typical vision and does not represent all forms of color vision variation

## Lab: Auditory sensation lab (sound waves and intensity)
- Links
  - https://phet.colorado.edu/en/simulations/sound-waves
  - https://phet.colorado.edu/sims/html/sound-waves/latest/sound-waves_all.html
- Activity type
  - Simulation with manipulable stimulus parameters
- Output type
  - frequency and amplitude changes with visible wave changes and audible changes
- Typical completion time
  - 10–20 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require a mapping statement
    - which control corresponds to pitch, which corresponds to loudness
  - Require one caution about device variability
    - speaker differences and volume settings limit comparability

## Lab: Hearing sensitivity curve lab (frequency response)
- Link
  - https://www.phys.unsw.edu.au/jw/hearing.html
- Activity type
  - Interactive hearing sensitivity test
- Output type
  - sensitivity curve or equal-loudness style output
- Typical completion time
  - 10–25 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Treat as a demonstration of frequency-dependent sensitivity, not a diagnostic audiogram
  - Require students to report their hardware conditions
    - headphones versus speakers and approximate volume setting
  - Require one validity limitation
    - lack of calibration and uncontrolled environment

## Teaching designs and ideas

## Option: 50-minute psychophysics lab day
- Part 1: One ISLE threshold method activity
- Part 2: One ISLE SDT activity
- Part 3: One PhET lab (Color Vision or Sound Waves) to connect stimulus parameters to sensory experience
- Wrap: one-page methods summary
  - IV, DV, operational definition, one confound, one fix

Grading artifact
- Two screenshots minimum
- One numeric estimate
- One short methods paragraph

## Option: Station rotation for mixed pacing
- Station 1: ISLE threshold method
- Station 2: ISLE SDT decision task
- Station 3: PhET Color Vision
- Station 4: PhET Sound Waves
- Station 5: UNSW hearing curve demo

Grading artifact
- One screenshot per station
- One sentence per station identifying IV and DV
- One limitation per station

## Option: Asynchronous lab with standardized prompts
- Students complete one ISLE activity and one PhET activity
- Students submit:
  - screenshots
  - one numeric output
  - three short answers
    - IV and DV
    - operational definition for the DV
    - one threat to validity and one mitigation

## Debrief prompts that keep this lab-like
- What was manipulated or what differed across trials
- What was measured and how was it operationalized
- How would a stricter or looser criterion change outcomes in SDT
- What sources of error are most likely in an online sensation lab
- What conclusion is justified and what conclusion would be overreach
---
```

```json
        "output_types": ["parameter_settings", "observable_outcome_change", "screenshot"],
        "typical_completion_time_minutes": { "min": 10, "max": 20 },
        "submission_evidence_format": ["screenshot", "short_reflection"],
        "submission_requirements": [
          "One screenshot showing the wave state after a parameter change",
          "One mapping statement: which control corresponds to pitch and loudness",
          "One limitation statement about device variability"
        ],
        "instructor_framing_notes": [
          "Require mapping between physical parameters and perception terms",
          "Require one device-variability limitation"
        ],
        "privacy_and_safety_notes": "Low risk. No personal disclosure required.",
        "opt_out_available": false
      },
      {
        "lab_id": "SENS-05",
        "lab_title": "Hearing sensitivity curve lab (frequency response)",
        "urls": ["https://www.phys.unsw.edu.au/jw/hearing.html"],
        "activity_type": "interactive_hearing_sensitivity_test",
        "output_types": ["graph_or_model_output", "screenshot"],
        "typical_completion_time_minutes": { "min": 10, "max": 25 },
        "submission_evidence_format": ["screenshot", "short_reflection"],
        "submission_requirements": [
          "Screenshot of the final curve or output",
          "Hardware condition note: headphones or speakers and approximate volume setting",
          "One validity limitation about calibration and environment control"
        ],
        "instructor_framing_notes": [
          "Frame as demonstration, not diagnosis",
          "Require explicit reporting of hardware conditions"
        ],
        "privacy_and_safety_notes": "Low to moderate risk if students interpret it as diagnosis. Provide a strong disclaimer and allow opt-out.",
        "opt_out_available": true,
        "opt_out_description": "Analyze an instructor-provided screenshot of a curve and answer the same interpretation prompts."
      }
    ],
    "teaching_designs_and_ideas": [
      {
        "design_id": "SENS-DESIGN-01",
        "design_name": "50-minute psychophysics lab day",
        "steps": [
          "Complete one ISLE threshold method activity",
          "Complete one ISLE SDT activity",
          "Complete one PhET activity (Color Vision or Sound Waves)",
          "Submit IV, DV, DV operational definition, one confound, one mitigation"
        ],
        "grading_artifact": ["two screenshots minimum", "one numeric estimate", "one short methods paragraph"]
      },
      {
        "design_id": "SENS-DESIGN-02",
        "design_name": "Station rotation for mixed pacing",
        "stations": [
          "ISLE threshold method",
          "ISLE SDT decision task",
          "PhET Color Vision",
          "PhET Sound Waves",
          "UNSW hearing curve demo"
        ],
        "grading_pattern": [
          "one screenshot per station",
          "one IV and DV sentence per station",
          "one limitation per station"
        ]
      },
      {
        "design_id": "SENS-DESIGN-03",
        "design_name": "Asynchronous lab with standardized prompts",
        "steps": [
          "Complete one ISLE activity and one PhET activity",
          "Submit screenshots, one numeric output, and three short answers: IV/DV, DV operational definition, one threat and one mitigation"
        ],
        "grading_artifact": ["screenshots", "one numeric output", "three short answers"]
      }
    ],
    "debrief_prompts": [
      "What was manipulated or what differed across trials",
      "What was measured and how was it operationalized",
      "How would a stricter or looser criterion change outcomes in SDT",
      "What sources of error are most likely in an online sensation lab",
      "What conclusion is justified and what conclusion would be overreach"
    ]
  }
}
```

### Block 67 (lang=markdown | source=md | block 67)

```markdown
---
title: "PSY-132 Interactive Teaching Labs: Perception"
filename: "psy-132-topic-8-perception-interactive-teaching-labs-free"
type: "resource_links"
status: "curated"
created: "2026-01-11"
updated: "2026-01-11"
origin: "Curated for PSY-132 Topic 8 with strict emphasis on free, student-facing interactive teaching labs that produce debriefable outputs (bistable perception, grouping judgments, depth cue manipulation, motion aftereffects, and attention-perception boundary effects)"
citation_style: "none"
verification_needed: true
tags:
  - "psy-132"
  - "perception"
  - "interactive-labs"
  - "free"
topics:
  - "Perception"
aliases: []
sources:
  - "https://isle.hanover.edu/Chapter05.html"
  - "https://isle.hanover.edu/isle2/index.html?ch=Chapter05"
  - "https://isle.hanover.edu/Chapter07.html"
  - "https://isle.hanover.edu/Chapter08.html"
  - "https://isle.hanover.edu/Chapter12.html"
  - "https://sites.socsci.uci.edu/~ddhoff/cb.html"
  - "https://michaelbach.de/ot/"
  - "https://michaelbach.de/ot/mot-adapt/"
  - "https://michaelbach.de/ot/mot-mib/"
cssclasses: []
notes: "Perception labs should be graded on predictions and evidence from interactive outputs. Avoid treating illusions as 'your brain is broken' narratives; frame them as evidence about normal perceptual inference. Click-test links before release."
---

## Selection rationale
- Perception is ideal for interactive labs because perceptual outputs are immediate and strongly debriefable
- Each activity produces recordable outputs suitable for grading at scale
  - screenshot of the illusion state or task outcome
  - a short prediction and whether it was supported
  - a brief mechanistic explanation using perception concepts
- All links are free and student-facing

## Interactive teaching labs

## Lab: Perceptual organization and object perception (Gestalt, figure-ground, illusory contours, bistable perception)
- Links
  - ISLE Chapter 5 hub
    - https://isle.hanover.edu/Chapter05.html
  - ISLE 2.0 Chapter 5 hub
    - https://isle.hanover.edu/isle2/index.html?ch=Chapter05
- Activity type
  - Interactive perception demonstrations and mini-experiments
- Output type
  - labeled perceptual phenomenon plus a short explanation
- Typical completion time
  - 15–30 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - short reflection
  - categorical output
- Instructor framing notes
  - Assign 3 specific activities so students produce comparable outputs
  - Require students to label the principle
    - figure-ground, proximity, similarity, closure, good continuation, common fate, illusory contours, bistable perception

## Lab: Depth perception and size constancy (cues and classic illusions)
- Link
  - ISLE Chapter 7 hub
    - https://isle.hanover.edu/Chapter07.html
- Activity type
  - Interactive depth and size activities
- Output type
  - cue manipulation plus observed perceptual change
- Typical completion time
  - 15–30 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require a monocular cue inventory for one activity
  - Require one statement distinguishing cue from inference

## Lab: Motion perception and aftereffects (adaptation as evidence)
- Link
  - ISLE Chapter 8 hub
    - https://isle.hanover.edu/Chapter08.html
- Activity type
  - Interactive motion perception tasks
- Output type
  - demonstration outcome plus an adaptation explanation
- Typical completion time
  - 10–25 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require students to write a prediction before adaptation and a report after adaptation
  - Require a mechanism statement referencing adaptation and opponent processing concepts where appropriate

## Lab: Speech perception as multisensory perception (integration and top-down effects)
- Link
  - ISLE Chapter 12 hub
    - https://isle.hanover.edu/Chapter12.html
- Activity type
  - Interactive speech perception activities
- Output type
  - perceptual judgment and a brief explanation
- Typical completion time
  - 10–25 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Assign one of:
    - McGurk effect, phonemic restoration, voicing onset time
  - Require a statement about multisensory integration or top-down reconstruction

## Lab: Attention–perception boundary (change blindness flicker task)
- Link
  - https://sites.socsci.uci.edu/~ddhoff/cb.html
- Activity type
  - Interactive change blindness demonstration
- Output type
  - whether the change was detected and what improved detection
- Typical completion time
  - 5–15 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require a procedural note
    - where they looked and what strategy helped
  - Require a limitation note
    - this is a demo and not a calibrated measure of attention

## Supplemental lab library: Visual phenomena and illusions (station options)
- Links
  - Index
    - https://michaelbach.de/ot/
  - Motion aftereffect
    - https://michaelbach.de/ot/mot-adapt/
  - Motion-induced blindness
    - https://michaelbach.de/ot/mot-mib/
- Activity type
  - Interactive illusion demonstrations with controlled viewing
- Output type
  - illusion state plus explanation of why perception diverges from stimulus
- Typical completion time
  - 5–15 minutes per station
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Assign specific illusions rather than letting students roam
  - Require one boundary condition
    - viewing distance, fixation, screen brightness, refresh rate can change effects

## Teaching designs and ideas

## Option: 50-minute lab day, “perception as inference”
- Part 1: One ISLE Chapter 5 activity on Gestalt organization
- Part 2: One ISLE Chapter 7 depth cue activity
- Part 3: Change blindness demo
- Wrap: One synthesis paragraph
  - “What does this tell us about perception being constructive rather than a camera”

Grading artifact
- Three screenshots
- One synthesis paragraph with two perception terms used correctly

## Option: Station rotation for mixed pacing
- Station 1: ISLE Chapter 5 (organization)
- Station 2: ISLE Chapter 7 (depth)
- Station 3: ISLE Chapter 8 (motion)
- Station 4: ISLE Chapter 12 (speech perception)
- Station 5: Change blindness

Grading artifact
- One screenshot per station
- One IV and DV statement per station
- One mechanism statement per station

## Option: Asynchronous online lab with standardized prompts
- Students complete:
  - one ISLE organization activity
  - one depth activity
  - one change blindness demo
- Students submit:
  - screenshots
  - three short answers
    - prediction
    - observation
    - mechanism explanation

## Debrief prompts that keep this lab-like
- What did you manipulate or what differed across conditions
- What did you perceive and how did it differ from the physical stimulus
- What inference is the perceptual system making in this situation
- What boundary condition changes the effect, such as fixation, distance, or context cues
- What conclusion is justified and what conclusion would be overreach
---
```

### Block 69 (lang=markdown | source=md | block 69)

```markdown
---
title: "PSY-132 Interactive Teaching Labs: Consciousness"
filename: "psy-132-topic-9-consciousness-interactive-teaching-labs-free"
type: "resource_links"
status: "curated"
created: "2026-01-11"
updated: "2026-01-11"
origin: "Curated for PSY-132 Topic 9 with strict emphasis on free, student-facing interactive teaching labs that produce debriefable outputs (reaction time lapses, sustained attention errors, chronotype measures, sleep quality scores, and structured sleep field data)"
citation_style: "none"
verification_needed: true
tags:
  - "psy-132"
  - "consciousness"
  - "interactive-labs"
  - "free"
topics:
  - "Consciousness"
aliases: []
sources:
  - "https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/pvtb.html"
  - "https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_pvtb.html"
  - "https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/mackworth.html"
  - "https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_mackworth.html"
  - "https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/sart.html"
  - "https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_sart.html"
  - "https://www.psytoolkit.org/survey-library/chronotype-cirens.html"
  - "https://jetlag.sleepopolis.com/"
  - "https://www.psytoolkit.org/survey-library/gsqs.html"
  - "https://www.psytoolkit.org/survey-library/sleep-quality-sqs.html"
  - "https://www.psytoolkit.org/survey-library/lseq.html"
  - "https://sleepeducation.org/resources/sleep-diary/"
  - "https://sleepeducation.org/docs/default-document-library/sleep-diary.pdf"
  - "https://learn.genetics.utah.edu/content/addiction/mouse/"
  - "https://learn.genetics.utah.edu/content/addiction/methmouse/"
cssclasses: []
notes: "Consciousness labs work best when they produce a measurable performance output or structured field data. Grade completion and methods reasoning, not ‘good sleep’ or personal disclosure. Click-test links before release."
---

## Selection rationale
- Consciousness is easiest to teach through measurable attention/vigilance tasks plus structured sleep and circadian measures
- These activities produce recordable outputs suitable for grading at scale
  - reaction time, lapses, and errors over time
  - chronotype and sleep-quality scores
  - sleep diary field data across days
- All links are free and student-facing

## Interactive teaching labs

## Lab: Vigilance and sleep loss effects (PVT-B)
- Links
  - PsyToolkit PVT-B overview
    - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/pvtb.html
  - PsyToolkit PVT-B run page
    - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_pvtb.html
- Activity type
  - Reaction-time vigilance task
- Output type
  - reaction time pattern and lapses
- Typical completion time
  - 5–10 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - numeric output
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require an operational DV statement
    - mean reaction time and number of lapses
  - Require a methods limitation statement
    - device latency, distractions, and time-of-day effects

## Lab: Sustained attention and mind-wandering (SART)
- Links
  - PsyToolkit SART overview
    - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/sart.html
  - PsyToolkit SART run page
    - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_sart.html
- Activity type
  - Sustained attention task
- Output type
  - commission errors and attention failures
- Typical completion time
  - 5–10 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - numeric output
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require a clear “what counts as an error” statement
  - Require one alternative explanation
    - misunderstanding instructions, speed–accuracy tradeoff, distractions

## Lab: Long-duration vigilance and rare-event detection (Mackworth Clock)
- Links
  - PsyToolkit Mackworth overview
    - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/mackworth.html
  - PsyToolkit Mackworth run page
    - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_mackworth.html
- Activity type
  - Vigilance task with rare targets
- Output type
  - detection misses and time-on-task decline pattern
- Typical completion time
  - 10–20 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - numeric output
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require a time-on-task hypothesis
    - “performance will decline over time”
  - Require one design improvement
    - counterbalancing time-of-day or controlling environment

## Lab: Circadian preference and chronotype (measurement lab)
- Link
  - PsyToolkit Chronotype Circadian Energy Scale (CIRENS)
    - https://www.psytoolkit.org/survey-library/chronotype-cirens.html
- Activity type
  - Scored self-report scale
- Output type
  - chronotype-related score profile
- Typical completion time
  - 5–10 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - numeric output
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Grade completion and measurement critique, not score direction
  - Require one validity limitation
    - self-report bias, week-to-week schedule differences, seasonal variation

## Lab: Jet lag and circadian phase shifting (interactive planning tool)
- Link
  - Jet Lag Rooster planner
    - https://jetlag.sleepopolis.com/
- Activity type
  - Input-driven schedule generator
- Output type
  - light and sleep timing recommendations under stated assumptions
- Typical completion time
  - 10–15 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Use a fictional travel scenario by default
  - Require students to list the assumptions the plan depends on

## Lab: Sleep quality measurement (scored scales)
- Links
  - PsyToolkit Groningen Sleep Quality Questionnaire (GSQS)
    - https://www.psytoolkit.org/survey-library/gsqs.html
  - PsyToolkit Sleep Quality Scale (SQS)
    - https://www.psytoolkit.org/survey-library/sleep-quality-sqs.html
  - PsyToolkit Leeds Sleep Evaluation Questionnaire (LSEQ)
    - https://www.psytoolkit.org/survey-library/lseq.html
- Activity type
  - Scored self-report scales
- Output type
  - total score or subscale scores
- Typical completion time
  - 5–15 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - numeric output
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Use vignette mode by default
    - score a provided “participant profile” instead of requiring personal disclosure
  - Require one measurement note
    - state versus trait, recall bias, and why a single night is not decisive

## Lab: Sleep diary field lab (structured data over time)
- Links
  - Sleep diary instructions
    - https://sleepeducation.org/resources/sleep-diary/
  - Two-week sleep diary PDF
    - https://sleepeducation.org/docs/default-document-library/sleep-diary.pdf
- Activity type
  - Field data collection
- Output type
  - daily sleep timing and quality entries
- Typical completion time
  - 2 minutes per day for 7–14 days
- Submission evidence format
  - completed diary (photo, scan, or typed transfer)
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Grade completeness and pattern interpretation, not “healthy sleep”
  - Require students to compute one derived variable
    - average sleep duration or variability in wake time

## Optional lab: Altered states through psychoactive drugs (interactive synapse model)
- Links
  - Mouse Party
    - https://learn.genetics.utah.edu/content/addiction/mouse/
  - Meth Mouse
    - https://learn.genetics.utah.edu/content/addiction/methmouse/
- Activity type
  - Interactive mechanism model
- Output type
  - mechanism description and predicted effects
- Typical completion time
  - 10–20 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Keep framing strictly educational and mechanism-focused
  - Avoid personal disclosure prompts and avoid “just say no” moralizing

## Teaching designs and ideas

## Option: 50-minute lab day, “attention over time”
- Part 1: PVT-B
- Part 2: SART
- Part 3: One short debrief comparing tasks
  - what each task measures and what each task confounds
- Wrap: one paragraph
  - IV, DV, and one validity threat for each task

Grading artifact
- Two screenshots
- Two numeric outputs
- One comparison paragraph

## Option: Station rotation for mixed pacing
- Station 1: PVT-B
- Station 2: SART
- Station 3: Chronotype (CIRENS)
- Station 4: Jet Lag Rooster (fictional scenario)
- Station 5: Sleep quality scale (vignette mode)

Grading artifact
- One screenshot per station
- One IV and DV statement per station
- One limitation per station

## Option: Asynchronous lab that generates a class dataset for Topic 4 later
- Students complete:
  - CIRENS score
  - one vigilance task metric (PVT-B mean RT or lapse count)
  - one week of diary-derived sleep duration estimate
- Instructor aggregates and uses later to discuss:
  - correlations, variability, and why causal inference is not justified

## Debrief prompts that keep this lab-like
- What is the independent variable or condition difference you are treating as meaningful
- What is the dependent variable and how is it operationalized
- What is one confound that is especially likely in online sleep and attention labs
- What claim is justified and what claim would be overreach
- What additional data would you need to make a stronger inference
---
```

### Block 71 (lang=markdown | source=md | block 71)

```markdown
---
title: "PSY-132 Interactive Teaching Labs: Learning"
filename: "psy-132-topic-10-learning-interactive-teaching-labs-free"
type: "resource_links"
status: "curated"
created: "2026-01-11"
updated: "2026-01-11"
origin: "Curated for PSY-132 Topic 10 with strict emphasis on free, student-facing interactive teaching labs that produce debriefable outputs (trial outcomes, parameter effects, schedules, and observable behavior change)"
citation_style: "none"
verification_needed: true
tags:
  - "psy-132"
  - "learning"
  - "interactive-labs"
  - "free"
topics:
  - "Learning"
aliases: []
sources:
  - "https://educationalgames.nobelprize.org/educational/medicine/pavlov/"
  - "https://educationalgames.nobelprize.org/educational/medicine/pavlov/pavlov.html"
  - "https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/rescrolawagner/"
  - "https://psych.hanover.edu/JavaTest/CLE/Cognition_js/RescorlaWagner/"
  - "https://studio.libretexts.org/h5p/15593"
  - "https://studio.libretexts.org/h5p/15594"
  - "https://studio.libretexts.org/h5p/15596"
  - "https://studio.libretexts.org/h5p/15599"
  - "https://studio.libretexts.org/h5p/15600"
  - "https://studio.libretexts.org/h5p/15602"
  - "https://studio.libretexts.org/h5p/5860"
  - "https://h5pstudio.ecampusontario.ca/fr/content/64358"
  - "https://epsych.msstate.edu/adaptive/Fuzz/index.html"
  - "https://studio.libretexts.org/h5p/15603"
cssclasses: []
notes: "Learning labs should be graded on operational definitions and evidence from outputs, not personal performance. Several links are older or platform-dependent, so click-test in your target student devices before release."
---

## Selection rationale
- Learning is most teachable when students can observe behavior change across trials, then explain it using specific learning terms
- These activities produce recordable outputs suitable for grading at scale
  - trial outcomes and visible behavior change
  - parameter-driven changes in predicted learning
  - schedule classification and contingency identification
- All links are free and student-facing

## Interactive teaching labs

## Lab: Classical conditioning in action (trial-based training)
- Links
  - Nobel Prize Pavlov game hub
    - https://educationalgames.nobelprize.org/educational/medicine/pavlov/
  - Direct play page
    - https://educationalgames.nobelprize.org/educational/medicine/pavlov/pavlov.html
- Activity type
  - Interactive game-as-experiment
- Output type
  - outcome across trials plus contingency description
- Typical completion time
  - 10–15 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require CS, US, CR, UR identification
  - Require one prediction about extinction or generalization

## Lab: Prediction error model of conditioning (Rescorla–Wagner parameter lab)
- Links
  - Rescorla–Wagner model page
    - https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/rescrolawagner/
  - JS simulation version
    - https://psych.hanover.edu/JavaTest/CLE/Cognition_js/RescorlaWagner/
- Activity type
  - Parameter manipulation simulation
- Output type
  - predicted associative strength changes under different salience and US settings
- Typical completion time
  - 10–25 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - two screenshots
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require students to change exactly one parameter and record the effect
  - Require a mechanism sentence in model terms
    - “Learning changes when prediction error changes”

## Lab: Classical conditioning concept checks (H5P interactive learning objects)
- Links
  - Classical Conditioning 6.2A
    - https://studio.libretexts.org/h5p/15593
  - Classical Conditioning 6.2B
    - https://studio.libretexts.org/h5p/15594
  - Classical Conditioning 6.2D
    - https://studio.libretexts.org/h5p/15596
- Activity type
  - H5P interactive activities
- Output type
  - completion evidence plus targeted concept application
- Typical completion time
  - 5–15 minutes per activity
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - categorical output
- Instructor framing notes
  - Assign one specific H5P object so students share the same prompt set
  - Require one “why this is the right label” justification sentence

## Lab: Operant conditioning concept checks (H5P interactive learning objects)
- Links
  - Operant Conditioning 6.3A
    - https://studio.libretexts.org/h5p/15599
  - Operant Conditioning 6.3B
    - https://studio.libretexts.org/h5p/15600
  - Operant Conditioning 6.3D
    - https://studio.libretexts.org/h5p/15602
  - Operant Conditioning Question Set 12.14A
    - https://studio.libretexts.org/h5p/5860
- Activity type
  - H5P interactive activities
- Output type
  - completion evidence plus contingency classification
- Typical completion time
  - 5–20 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - categorical output
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require students to label
    - positive reinforcement, negative reinforcement, positive punishment, negative punishment
  - Require a one-sentence “behavior change direction” statement
    - increase or decrease the target behavior

## Lab: Schedules of reinforcement classification (Drag the Words)
- Link
  - eCampusOntario H5P “Examples of schedules of reinforcement”
    - https://h5pstudio.ecampusontario.ca/fr/content/64358
- Activity type
  - H5P drag-and-drop classification
- Output type
  - completion evidence and correct schedule labels
- Typical completion time
  - 5–10 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - categorical output
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require students to translate schedule labels into a plain-language example
    - one example each for FR, VR, FI, VI

## Lab: Operant conditioning as a shaping simulation (legacy interactive)
- Link
  - ePsych “Fuzz” Operant Conditioning
    - https://epsych.msstate.edu/adaptive/Fuzz/index.html
- Activity type
  - Interactive shaping-style simulation
- Output type
  - observed behavior change under reinforcement and punishment conditions
- Typical completion time
  - 10–25 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require a procedural record
    - what the student reinforced and what changed
  - Require one limitation statement
    - this is not a controlled lab measure and may behave differently across devices

## Lab: Observational learning (modeling) concept application (H5P)
- Link
  - Observational Learning (Modeling) 6.4A
    - https://studio.libretexts.org/h5p/15603
- Activity type
  - H5P interactive activity
- Output type
  - completion evidence plus concept application
- Typical completion time
  - 5–15 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - screenshot
  - short reflection
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require students to name the conditions that increase modeling
    - attention, retention, reproduction, motivation

## Safety and privacy defaults for this topic
- Grade completion and concept reasoning, not performance level
- Avoid requiring students to disclose personal behavior change goals
- Use fictional scenarios when asking for examples

## Teaching designs and ideas

## Option: 50-minute “learning mechanisms” lab day
- Part 1: Pavlov game
- Part 2: Rescorla–Wagner parameter change
- Part 3: One operant H5P activity
- Wrap: one-page learning audit
  - learning type, IV, DV, operational definition, predicted change, one limitation

Grading artifact
- Three screenshots
- One short audit page

## Option: Station rotation for mixed pacing
- Station 1: Classical conditioning H5P
- Station 2: Operant conditioning H5P
- Station 3: Schedules H5P
- Station 4: Pavlov game
- Station 5: Rescorla–Wagner simulation

Grading artifact
- One screenshot per station
- One label plus one justification sentence per station

## Option: Hypothesis-first mini-study inside Topic 10
- Pre-specify
  - “Changing salience will change acquisition speed in the Rescorla–Wagner model”
- Students run two conditions
  - one baseline, one salience change
- Students submit
  - two screenshots and one comparison sentence

## Debrief prompts that keep this lab-like
- What is the independent variable in this activity
- What is the dependent variable and how is it operationalized
- What pattern across trials counts as evidence of learning
- What alternative explanation could produce the same pattern
- What conclusion is justified and what conclusion would be overreach
---
```
