### Block 73 (lang=markdown | source=md | block 73)

```markdown
---
title: "PSY-132 Interactive Teaching Labs: Memory"
filename: "psy-132-topic-11-memory-interactive-teaching-labs-free"
type: "resource_links"
status: "curated"
created: "2026-01-11"
updated: "2026-01-11"
origin: "Curated for PSY-132 Topic 11 with strict emphasis on free, student-facing interactive teaching labs that produce debriefable outputs (span, accuracy, reaction time, serial position patterns, and false memory effects)"
citation_style: "none"
verification_needed: true
tags:
  - "psy-132"
  - "memory"
  - "interactive-labs"
  - "free"
topics:
  - "Memory"
aliases: []
sources:
  - "https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/"
  - "https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/cognition.html"
  - "https://studies.testmybrain.org/m2c2/?study=m2c2"
cssclasses: []
notes: "Memory labs should be graded on evidence, measurement, and interpretation. Avoid grading students on performance level. Click-test links before release."
---

## Selection rationale
- Memory is naturally lab-driven because performance is observable and quantifiable
- These activities produce recordable outputs suitable for grading at scale
  - maximum span, accuracy, reaction time summaries, serial position patterns, false memory indicators
- All links are free and student-facing

## Core lab hubs you can reuse all semester

- PsyToolkit Experiment Library
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/
  - Best for classic cognitive tasks with in-browser results screens

- Hanover Cognition Laboratory Experiments (HTML5/JS hub)
  - https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/cognition.html
  - Best when you want “lab day” structure, parameter manipulation, and repeatable demonstrations

- TestMyBrain Memory Games (M2C2 battery)
  - https://studies.testmybrain.org/m2c2/?study=m2c2
  - Best as a quick participation-based battery with a clear end state for submission

## Interactive teaching labs

## Lab: Working memory span (verbal and visuospatial)
- PsyToolkit Digit Span (run)
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_digitspan.html
- PsyToolkit Reverse Digit Span (run)
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_rdigitspan.html
- PsyToolkit Corsi Block-Tapping (run)
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_corsi.html
- PsyToolkit Backward Corsi (run)
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_backward_corsi.html

Output you can grade
- Maximum span (one number) and one screenshot of the results screen

Instructor framing notes
- Require a distinction between the construct and the measure
  - “Span score is a performance measure that approximates working memory capacity under specific task demands”
- Require one likely confound in online testing
  - distraction, misunderstanding instructions, device differences

## Lab: Updating and working memory load (N-back)
- PsyToolkit 2-Back (run)
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_nback2.html
- PsyToolkit 2-Back touchscreen version (run)
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/touch_nback2.html

Output you can grade
- Accuracy or score summary (if shown) plus a screenshot

Instructor framing notes
- Require a prediction before running
  - “Performance should drop if the task is harder or if attention is divided”
- Require a speed–accuracy note
  - why faster responding can increase errors

## Lab: Complex span and dual-task demands (operation span)
- PsyToolkit Automated Operation Span (run)
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_aospan.html

Output you can grade
- Final score plus a screenshot

Instructor framing notes
- Require a plain-language description of the two tasks happening at once
- Require a claim about why dual-tasking stresses working memory

## Lab: Interference and short-term memory loss (Brown–Peterson style)
- Hanover Brown–Peterson interference lab
  - https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/BrownPeterson.html

Output you can grade
- One screenshot of results plus one sentence identifying the interference mechanism

Instructor framing notes
- Require a distinction between decay and interference as explanations
- Require a limitation statement
  - uncontrolled environment, practice effects, and device variability

## Lab: Serial position (primacy and recency) as a class dataset
- Hanover Serial Position lab
  - https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/SerialPosition.html

Output you can grade
- One screenshot of the serial position pattern
- Two derived values
  - average recall for early items and late items (students can estimate or compute if the tool displays counts)

Instructor framing notes
- Require an interpretation that links primacy and recency to memory processes
- Require an “analysis caution” note
  - distribution shape and ceiling effects can distort simple averages

## Lab: False memory (DRM paradigm demonstration)
- Hanover DRM False Memory lab
  - https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/DRMfalseMemory.html

Output you can grade
- One screenshot plus one “false memory indicator” statement
  - for example, whether the critical lure was endorsed

Instructor framing notes
- Require careful phrasing
  - this demonstrates normal memory reconstruction under specific conditions
- Require an ethics note
  - why this should not be used to judge credibility in real-life settings

## Optional lab: Quick battery participation (TestMyBrain)
- TestMyBrain Memory Games (M2C2)
  - https://studies.testmybrain.org/m2c2/?study=m2c2

Output you can grade
- Completion evidence screenshot plus one short reflection about task difficulty and measurement noise

Instructor framing notes
- Grade completion and methodological reflection only
- Do not treat results as diagnostic or stable traits

## Safety and privacy defaults for this topic
- Grade completion, interpretation, and methods reasoning, not performance level
- Allow an opt-out alternative
  - analyze an instructor-provided screenshot of results and answer the same prompts

## Teaching designs and ideas

## Option: 50-minute lab day, “how memory fails”
- Part 1: Digit Span or Corsi (working memory)
- Part 2: Brown–Peterson (interference)
- Part 3: DRM false memory (reconstruction)
- Wrap: one-page methods note
  - what was measured, what could bias it, and what claim is justified

Grading artifact
- Three screenshots
- One paragraph explaining the three different failure mechanisms

## Option: Station rotation that produces a reusable class dataset
- Station 1: Digit Span
- Station 2: N-back
- Station 3: Serial Position
- Station 4: DRM False Memory

Grading artifact
- One screenshot per station
- One numeric output per station
- One limitation statement per station

## Debrief prompts that keep this lab-like
- What was measured and how was it operationalized
- What pattern counts as evidence of a memory effect, not just random variation
- What alternative explanation could produce the same pattern
- What online-lab confound is most plausible and how would you mitigate it
- What conclusion is justified and what conclusion would be overreach
---
```

```json
    "debrief_prompts": [
      "What was measured and how was it operationalized",
      "What pattern counts as evidence of a memory effect rather than random variation",
      "What alternative explanation could produce the same pattern",
      "What online-lab confound is most plausible and how would you mitigate it",
      "What conclusion is justified and what conclusion would be overreach"
    ]
  }
}
```

### Block 75 (lang=markdown | source=md | block 75)

```markdown
---
title: "PSY-132 Interactive Teaching Labs: Cognition"
filename: "psy-132-topic-12-cognition-interactive-teaching-labs-free"
type: "resource_links"
status: "curated"
created: "2026-01-11"
updated: "2026-01-11"
origin: "Curated for PSY-132 Topic 12 with strict emphasis on free, student-facing interactive teaching labs that produce debriefable outputs (reaction time, accuracy, switching costs, interference effects, search slopes, and decision patterns)"
citation_style: "none"
verification_needed: true
tags:
  - "psy-132"
  - "cognition"
  - "interactive-labs"
  - "free"
topics:
  - "Cognition"
aliases: []
sources:
  - "https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/"
  - "https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/cognition.html"
  - "https://www.philosophyexperiments.com/wason/Default.aspx"
  - "https://www.philosophyexperiments.com/wason/Default2.aspx"
  - "https://www.philosophyexperiments.com/wason/Default3.aspx"
  - "https://montyhall.io/"
cssclasses: []
notes: "Cognition labs should be graded on evidence and reasoning, not performance. Many tasks are sensitive to distraction and device differences; require limitation statements. Click-test links before release."
---

## Selection rationale
- Cognition is highly teachable through lab tasks because core constructs appear as measurable performance patterns
- These activities produce recordable outputs suitable for grading at scale
  - reaction time and accuracy
  - condition differences such as congruent versus incongruent
  - switching costs and time-on-task decline
  - decision patterns that reveal reasoning traps
- All links are free and student-facing

## Core lab hubs you can reuse all semester
- PsyToolkit Experiment Library
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/
- Hanover Cognition Laboratory Experiments (HTML5/JS hub)
  - https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/cognition.html

## Interactive teaching labs

## Lab: Selective attention and interference (Stroop)
- PsyToolkit Stroop (run)
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_stroop.html
- Hanover Stroop (HTML5/JS)
  - https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/stroop.html

Output you can grade
- Screenshot of results
- One difference score if available, such as incongruent minus congruent

Instructor framing notes
- Require a processing explanation referencing automaticity and interference
- Require a speed–accuracy caution statement

## Lab: Executive attention and distractor interference (Flanker)
- PsyToolkit Flanker (run)
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_flanker.html
- PsyToolkit Flanker arrows (alternative)
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/flanker_arrows.html

Output you can grade
- Screenshot plus one condition difference statement
- One limitation statement about distractions and device latency

Instructor framing notes
- Require a clear identification of the congruent and incongruent conditions

## Lab: Cognitive flexibility (task switching and multitasking)
- PsyToolkit Task Switching (run)
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_taskswitching.html
- PsyToolkit Multitasking (run)
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_multitasking.html

Output you can grade
- Screenshot of results
- One qualitative report of switch cost or multitask cost

Instructor framing notes
- Require an operational definition of switching cost
  - performance difference between switch and repeat trials

## Lab: Response inhibition (Go/No-go and Stop Signal)
- PsyToolkit Go/No-go (run)
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_go-no-go.html
- PsyToolkit Stop Signal (run)
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_stopsignal.html

Output you can grade
- Screenshot plus one error metric
  - commission errors or stop failures

Instructor framing notes
- Require a “what counts as an error” statement
- Require one design improvement suggestion to reduce confounds

## Lab: Temporal attention bottleneck (attentional blink)
- PsyToolkit Attentional Blink (run)
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_ab.html
- Hanover Attentional Blink (HTML5/JS)
  - https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/attnBlink.html

Output you can grade
- Screenshot plus one sentence describing the bottleneck effect

Instructor framing notes
- Require a prediction before running and a report after running

## Lab: Divided attention and cognitive load (dual task)
- Hanover Dual Task (HTML5/JS)
  - https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/dualTask.html

Output you can grade
- Screenshot plus one statement comparing single-task and dual-task performance

Instructor framing notes
- Require an explanation of limited-capacity processing

## Lab: Visual search (set size effects)
- PsyToolkit Visual Search (run)
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_search.html

Output you can grade
- Screenshot plus a “search slope” interpretation statement
  - how performance changes when more items are added

Instructor framing notes
- Require a prediction: parallel search versus serial search under different conditions

## Lab: Reasoning trap (Wason selection task)
- Philosophy Experiments Wason series
  - Q1: https://www.philosophyexperiments.com/wason/Default.aspx
  - Q2: https://www.philosophyexperiments.com/wason/Default2.aspx
  - Q3: https://www.philosophyexperiments.com/wason/Default3.aspx

Output you can grade
- Selected cards plus one explanation of why that selection tests the rule

Instructor framing notes
- Require explicit statement of falsification logic, not confirmation logic

## Lab: Decision making under uncertainty (Monty Hall)
- Interactive simulator
  - https://montyhall.io/

Output you can grade
- A brief record of results across at least 10 trials
  - stay versus switch win rates

Instructor framing notes
- Require a probability explanation and one reason intuition fails here

## Safety and privacy defaults for this topic
- Grade completion and reasoning, not performance level
- Require a limitation statement for every task
- Offer an opt-out path
  - analyze an instructor-provided screenshot and answer the same IV/DV prompts

## Teaching designs and ideas

## Option: 50-minute “where cognition breaks” lab day
- Part 1: Stroop or Flanker
- Part 2: Task Switching
- Part 3: Monty Hall
- Wrap: one-page synthesis
  - which tasks reflect interference, which reflect capacity limits, which reflect probabilistic reasoning

Grading artifact
- Three screenshots
- One synthesis paragraph with three cognition terms used correctly

## Option: Station rotation for mixed pacing
- Station 1: Stroop
- Station 2: Go/No-go
- Station 3: Attentional blink
- Station 4: Visual search
- Station 5: Wason or Monty Hall

Grading artifact
- One screenshot per station
- One IV and DV sentence per station
- One limitation per station

## Debrief prompts that keep this lab-like
- What is the independent variable or condition difference
- What is the dependent variable and how is it quantified
- What pattern counts as evidence of the cognitive construct
- What confound is most likely in online testing and how would you mitigate it
- What conclusion is justified and what conclusion would be overreach
---
```

### Block 77 (lang=markdown | source=md | block 77)

```markdown
---
title: "PSY-132 Interactive Teaching Labs: Topics 1–3"
filename: "psy-132-topics-1-3-interactive-teaching-labs-free"

notes: "Pack includes Topic 1 History, Topic 2 Theoretical Perspectives, Topic 3 Research Methods. All links are intended to support lab-style interactivity with debriefable outputs and low-cost grading artifacts."
---

## Topic 1: History

## Selection rationale
- Free, browser-based resources that students actively navigate, classify, and extract evidence from
- Activities produce recordable outputs suitable for grading at scale
- Designed to support debriefs about how the field changed over time and why

## Interactive teaching labs

## Interactive timeline scavenger hunt (Annenberg Learner)
- Link
  - https://www.learner.org/series/discovering-psychology/explorations/history-of-psychology-contemporary-foundations/
- Activity type
  - Interactive timeline exploration
- Output type
  - Coded event selections and short written evidence claims
- Typical completion time
  - 10–20 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - Screenshot of two selected timeline entries
  - Three-item response set: date, person or concept, why it matters
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require students to label each entry as one of: method shift, theory shift, institutional milestone, applied use case

## Interactive institutional timeline (APA History and Archives)
- Link
  - https://www.apa.org/about/apa/archives/timeline
- Activity type
  - Interactive timeline with milestone filtering
- Output type
  - Event selection plus classification code
- Typical completion time
  - 10–15 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - Screenshot of one milestone
  - One-paragraph context note using only what is on the page
- Instructor framing notes
  - Use to teach the difference between psychology as a science and psychology as a profession

## Online exhibits with built-in classroom activities (Cummings Center, University of Akron)
- Link
  - https://www.uakron.edu/chp/education/online-exhibits
- Activity type
  - Curated exhibit plus attached teaching resources
- Output type
  - Scavenger hunt answers and primary-source evidence extraction
- Typical completion time
  - 20–30 minutes per exhibit
- Submission evidence format
  - One completed scavenger hunt page or answer set
  - One source card with: artifact title, what it is, what claim it supports
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require students to separate description from interpretation

## Museum scavenger hunt as a structured history lab (National Museum of Psychology)
- Core museum page
  - https://www.uakron.edu/chp/museum/
- Scavenger hunt PDF
  - https://www.uakron.edu/chp/images/ScavengerHunt_short_final2018.pdf
- Educator guide PDF
  - https://www.uakron.edu/chp/museum/A%20Guide%20for%20Educators_National%20Museum%20of%20Psychology%20-%202022%20Edit.pdf?language_id=1
- Activity type
  - Guided artifact search and matching task
- Output type
  - Completed matching and short-response prompts
- Typical completion time
  - 20–40 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - Photo or scan of completed scavenger hunt page
  - One supported claim about an exhibit using evidence visible in the materials
- Instructor framing notes
  - Works in-person or virtual if you provide screenshots of a few exhibits

## Curated collection lab (Smithsonian Learning Lab)
- Link
  - https://learninglab.si.edu/collections/exploring-heredity-race-eugenics-and-the-history-of-intelligence-testing/ytlaOzLVuq36ejHP
- Activity type
  - Curated collection navigation and annotation
- Output type
  - Item selection plus evidence-based critique
- Typical completion time
  - 20–30 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - Select two items and submit a two-column analysis: what it is; what claim it supports or complicates
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require a bias and ethics note: plausible misuse and harm pathway

## Artifact analysis lab (Barnard Psychology Virtual Museum)
- Link
  - https://psychology.barnard.edu/psych-psych-virtual-museum
- Activity type
  - Artifact browsing and structured analysis
- Output type
  - Instrument inference worksheet
- Typical completion time
  - 15–25 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - Choose one apparatus and answer: what it is; what it might measure; what assumption it embeds; what would count as evidence
- Instructor framing notes
  - Bridge directly into Topic 3 Research Methods

## Micro-history lessons with scavenger hunts (Cummings Center 5 Minute History Lessons)
- Hub
  - https://www.uakron.edu/chp/education/videos.dot
- Example teacher guide PDF
  - https://www.uakron.edu/chp/education/pdfs/Episode7_TeachersGuide_5MHL.pdf
- Activity type
  - Short video plus scavenger hunt and discussion prompts
- Output type
  - Completed scavenger hunt plus one synthesis claim
- Typical completion time
  - 15–25 minutes
- Submission evidence format
  - Completed scavenger hunt answers and one sentence linking the episode to a broader trend

## Teaching designs and ideas
- One 50-minute history-as-evidence lab day
  - Annenberg timeline scavenger hunt
  - One Akron online exhibit with teaching prompts
  - One methods statement: how did psychology try to make its claims credible in this era
- Station rotation
  - Annenberg timeline, APA timeline, Akron exhibit, Barnard apparatus analysis, Smithsonian collection
- Asynchronous lab
  - One exhibit-based lab plus a source card and a historical-assumption paragraph

## Debrief prompts
- What changed over time that can function as an independent variable
- What counts as evidence in this era
- What alternative explanation could also account for the shift
- What ethical hazard follows from misuse

---

## Topic 2: Theoretical Perspectives

## Selection rationale
- Perspectives are conceptual lenses, so the most teachable lab format is repeated exposure to mini-activities that produce an output and then require perspective mapping
- Each activity produces a recordable output: score, reaction-time effect, decision pattern, plotted trend, or saved values profile
- All links are free and student-facing

## Interactive teaching labs

## Biological perspective lab (neural mechanisms)
- Link
  - https://phet.colorado.edu/sims/html/neuron/latest/neuron_en.html
- Output
  - Screenshot plus a variable-change note

## Behavioral perspective lab (classical conditioning)
- Link
  - https://educationalgames.nobelprize.org/educational/medicine/pavlov/pavlov.html
- Output
  - Screenshot plus CS, US, CR, UR identification

## Cognitive perspective lab (interference and automaticity)
- Link
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_stroop.html
- Output
  - Screenshot plus congruent versus incongruent performance difference if shown

## Nonconscious processing bridge lab (timed categorization)
- Link
  - https://implicit.harvard.edu/implicit/takeatest.html
- Output
  - Completion evidence plus a methods limitation sentence
- Instructor framing notes
  - Frame as automatic cognition and nonconscious processes, not as a diagnostic interpretation

## Evolutionary perspective lab (strategic interaction and cooperation)
- Link
  - https://ncase.me/trust/
- Output
  - One screenshot of an outcome plus a “what worked and why” strategy note

## Sociocultural perspective lab (context and systems via data)
- Link
  - https://www.gapminder.org/fw/world-health-chart/
- Output
  - Screenshot of a country comparison plus one confound hypothesis
- Instructor framing notes
  - Require group-level language and ecological fallacy avoidance

## Humanistic perspective lab (values, meaning, choice)
- Link
  - https://www.valuescardsort.com/
- Output
  - Screenshot or exported output plus one sentence explaining a top value using a fictional scenario

## Capstone multi-perspective comparison (explicitly contrasts approaches)
- Link
  - https://www.learner.org/series/discovering-psychology/explorations/approaches-in-practice/
- Output
  - An approach match table: perspective, key assumption, best-fit evidence

## Teaching designs and ideas
- 50-minute station rotation
  - Pavlov, Stroop, Neuron, Gapminder
  - Wrap with a perspective match table
- Hypothesis-first mini-study
  - Run Stroop or Neuron
  - Submit output, prediction, and perspective justification

## Debrief prompts
- What is the dependent variable in the activity
- Which mechanism does each perspective claim explains the output
- What a different perspective would treat as the key variable
- What is one limitation of single-lens interpretation

---

## Topic 3: Research Methods

## Selection rationale
- Research methods is easiest to teach by running small experiments and then forcing students to name variables and validity threats
- Each activity produces recordable outputs suitable for online-lab grading at scale
- All links are free and student-facing in a browser

## Core lab hubs
- PsyToolkit Experiment Library
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/
- Hanover Cognition Laboratory Experiments (HTML5/JS hub)
  - https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/cognition.html
- Web Experimental Psychology Lab (Konstanz archive hub)
  - https://iscience.uni-konstanz.de/archive/ulf/Lab/WebExpPsyLab.html
- Understanding Science interactive
  - https://undsci.berkeley.edu/for-educators/find-lessons-and-tools/how-science-works-interactive/
- Build-your-own experiment tools
  - https://lab.js.org/
  - https://labjs.felixhenninger.com/
  - https://www.jspsych.org/
  - https://github.com/jspsych/experiment-demos

## Interactive teaching labs

## Run an RT experiment and extract IV and DV
- PsyToolkit Stroop
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_stroop.html
- PsyToolkit Flanker
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_flanker.html
- Output
  - Screenshot, difference score if shown, IV/DV/confound paragraph

## Measurement and reliability planning (Digit Span)
- PsyToolkit Digit Span
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_digitspan.html
- Output
  - Score plus a test–retest plan

## Parameter manipulation and optional CSV export
- Hanover Mental Rotation
  - https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/mentRot.html
- Hanover Stroop
  - https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/stroop.html
- Output
  - Screenshot of settings and results, prediction-before and interpretation-after

## Subject pool and sampling critique
- Web Experimental Psychology Lab hub
  - https://iscience.uni-konstanz.de/archive/ulf/Lab/WebExpPsyLab.html
- Output
  - Methods audit card: task, what was measured, implied sampling, bias risk

## Science workflow documentation
- How Science Works interactive
  - https://undsci.berkeley.edu/for-educators/find-lessons-and-tools/how-science-works-interactive/
- Output
  - Screenshot of a completed workflow artifact with a rival hypothesis and boundary condition

## Build-your-own micro-experiment
- lab.js Builder
  - https://labjs.felixhenninger.com/
- jsPsych demos
  - https://github.com/jspsych/experiment-demos
- Output
  - One runnable task design plus a short method section

## Teaching designs and ideas
- 50-minute IV/DV bootcamp
  - Run one RT task
  - Submit IV, DV, operational definition, confound, mitigation
- Station rotation
  - Stroop, Digit Span, Mental Rotation with one parameter change, workflow artifact
- Mini-study proposal
  - Choose feasible IV and write hypothesis, operational definitions, planned analysis, threat and mitigation

## Debrief prompts
- What is the independent variable and its levels
- What is the dependent variable and how is it quantified
- What alternative explanation competes with your preferred interpretation
- What online-lab confound is most likely and how to mitigate it
- What conclusion is justified and what conclusion is overreach
---
```

```json
            ],

          },
```

```markdown
---

  - "https://quandarygame.org/play"
cssclasses: []
notes: "Pack includes Topic 4 Statistics and Topic 5 Ethics. Both are constrained to free, student-facing interactive teaching labs with debriefable outputs and grading-friendly artifacts."
---

## Topic 4: Statistics

## Selection rationale
- Statistics is best learned by simulation and interactive visualization rather than formula-first instruction
- Each activity produces recordable outputs suitable for grading at scale
  - screenshot of a graph or distribution
  - one numeric result such as confidence interval endpoints or p-value estimate
  - one plain-language interpretation with a limitation
- All links are free and student-facing

## Interactive teaching labs
- StatKey bootstrap confidence intervals
  - https://www.lock5stat.com/StatKey/
  - https://www.lock5stat.com/StatKey/bootstrap_1_quant/bootstrap_1_quant.html
- StatKey randomization test for a difference
  - https://www.lock5stat.com/StatKey/randomization_1_quant_1_cat/randomization_1_quant_1_cat.html
- OnlineStatBook sampling distributions simulation
  - https://onlinestatbook.com/stat_sim/sampling_dist/
  - https://onlinestatbook.com/stat_sim/samp_dist_js/index.html
- Rossman/Chance Guess the Correlation
  - https://www.rossmanchance.com/applets/GuessCorrelation.html
- CODAP data analysis environment
  - https://codap.concord.org/
  - https://codap.concord.org/get-started/
- Tuva Tools tutorials and tools
  - https://tuvalabs.com/tools/
  - https://tuvalabs.com/tutorials/
- Gapminder World Health Chart
  - https://www.gapminder.org/fw/world-health-chart/
- Optional: Seeing Theory interactive concept visuals
  - https://seeing-theory.brown.edu/

## Teaching designs and ideas
- 50-minute inference lab day
  - Sampling distributions, then StatKey bootstrap interval, then interpretation paragraph
- Station rotation
  - Guess correlation, sampling distributions, StatKey, CODAP
- Asynchronous dataset builder
  - Students submit one StatKey numeric result plus screenshot; instructor aggregates for distribution discussion

## Debrief prompts
- What is the statistic and what is being treated as the sample
- What does the output represent
- What claim is justified and what claim would be overreach
- What would change with larger sample or noisier measurement
- What confound or bias could distort interpretation

---

## Topic 5: Ethics

## Selection rationale
- Ethics is most teachable through decision points and consequence tracing rather than lecture-only coverage
- Each activity produces recordable outputs suitable for grading at scale
  - decision path and outcome
  - completion evidence and a methods reflection
  - quiz completion where available
- All links are free and student-facing

## Interactive teaching labs
- ORI The Lab
  - https://ori.hhs.gov/the-lab
- ORI Research Clinic
  - https://ori.hhs.gov/research-clinic
- OHRP Participant-Centered Informed Consent Training
  - https://www.hhs.gov/ohrp/education-and-outreach/human-research-protection-training/participant-centered-informed-consent-training/index.html
- OpenLearn ethics committee challenge
  - https://www.open.edu/openlearn/society-politics-law/why-do-we-need-research-ethics
- MIT Moral Machine
  - https://moralmachine.mit.edu/
- UPenn MEHP ethics of research with human subjects module
  - https://improvinghealthcare.mehp.upenn.edu/course/ethics-research-human-subjects
- Optional: Quandary ethics game
  - https://quandarygame.org/play

## Teaching designs and ideas
- 50-minute research ethics lab day
  - ORI scenario plus consent critique plus one-page ethics audit
- Station rotation
  - ORI, OpenLearn, Moral Machine, consent critique
- Asynchronous standardized prompts
  - One activity plus screenshot plus three short answers: decision, principle, missing info

## Debrief prompts
- What was the decision point and available options
- What foreseeable consequences followed each option
- What ethical principle or rule did you prioritize and why
- What information was missing that would change the decision
- What mitigation would reduce harm while preserving the research question
---
```

### Block 81 (lang=markdown | source=md | block 81)

```markdown
---
title: "PSY-132 Interactive Teaching Labs: Topics 7–8"
filename: "psy-132-topics-7-8-interactive-teaching-labs-free"
type: "resource_links_pack"
status: "curated"
created: "2026-01-11"
updated: "2026-01-11"
origin: "Combined pack of Topic 7 Sensation and Topic 8 Perception interactive teaching lab link sets, constrained to free, student-facing, lab-style interactivity"
citation_style: "none"
verification_needed: true
tags:
  - "psy-132"
  - "interactive-labs"
  - "free"
  - "topics-7-8"
topics:
  - "Sensation"
  - "Perception"
aliases: []
sources:
  - "https://isle.hanover.edu/Chapter02.html"
  - "https://isle.hanover.edu/isle2/index.html?ch=Chapter02"
  - "https://phet.colorado.edu/en/simulations/color-vision"
  - "https://phet.colorado.edu/sims/html/color-vision/latest/color-vision_en.html"
  - "https://phet.colorado.edu/en/simulations/sound-waves"
  - "https://phet.colorado.edu/sims/html/sound-waves/latest/sound-waves_all.html"
  - "https://www.phys.unsw.edu.au/jw/hearing.html"
  - "https://isle.hanover.edu/Chapter05.html"
  - "https://isle.hanover.edu/isle2/index.html?ch=Chapter05"
  - "https://isle.hanover.edu/Chapter07.html"
  - "https://isle.hanover.edu/Chapter08.html"
  - "https://isle.hanover.edu/Chapter12.html"
  - "https://sites.socsci.uci.edu/~ddhoff/cb.html"
  - "https://michaelbach.de/ot/"
  - "https://michaelbach.de/ot/mot-adapt/"
  - "https://michaelbach.de/ot/mot-mib/"
cssclasses: []
notes: "Pack includes Topic 7 Sensation and Topic 8 Perception. Both emphasize lab-style interactivity (measurement, manipulation, and debriefable outputs). Grade operational definitions, predictions, and limitations rather than performance level."
---

## Topic 7: Sensation

## Selection rationale
- Sensation is measurement-first, so the best teaching labs are psychophysics and signal detection tasks with recordable outputs.
- Outputs are grading-friendly: threshold estimates, SDT outcomes, ROC shifts, and parameter-change screenshots.

## Core interactive labs (free)
- ISLE Chapter 2 psychophysics hub (thresholds, JND, SDT, ROC)
  - https://isle.hanover.edu/Chapter02.html
  - https://isle.hanover.edu/isle2/index.html?ch=Chapter02
- PhET Color Vision (stimulus parameter manipulation)
  - https://phet.colorado.edu/en/simulations/color-vision
  - https://phet.colorado.edu/sims/html/color-vision/latest/color-vision_en.html
- PhET Sound Waves (frequency and amplitude manipulation)
  - https://phet.colorado.edu/en/simulations/sound-waves
  - https://phet.colorado.edu/sims/html/sound-waves/latest/sound-waves_all.html
- UNSW online hearing sensitivity demonstration (calibration-limited; requires strong disclaimer)
  - https://www.phys.unsw.edu.au/jw/hearing.html

## Teaching design ideas
- 50-minute lab day
  - One ISLE threshold method activity
  - One ISLE SDT or ROC activity
  - One PhET activity (color or sound)
  - Submit IV, DV, DV operational definition, one confound, one mitigation
- Station rotation
  - ISLE threshold, ISLE SDT, PhET color, PhET sound, optional UNSW hearing curve
- Submission pattern (scales well)
  - One screenshot plus one numeric estimate plus one limitation statement per station

## Debrief prompts
- What was manipulated or what differed across trials?
- What was measured and how was it operationalized?
- How would a stricter or looser criterion change SDT outcomes?
- What online-lab confound is most plausible here?
- What conclusion is justified and what is overreach?

---

## Topic 8: Perception

## Selection rationale
- Perception labs are strongest when students make predictions, experience a perceptual outcome, and explain it as inference under constraints.
- Outputs are grading-friendly: screenshots, labeled phenomena, prediction-versus-observation notes, and boundary-condition statements.

## Core interactive labs (free)
- ISLE Chapter 5 (Gestalt, figure-ground, illusory contours, bistable perception)
  - https://isle.hanover.edu/Chapter05.html
  - https://isle.hanover.edu/isle2/index.html?ch=Chapter05
- ISLE Chapter 7 (depth cues and constancies)
  - https://isle.hanover.edu/Chapter07.html
- ISLE Chapter 8 (motion perception and aftereffects)
  - https://isle.hanover.edu/Chapter08.html
- ISLE Chapter 12 (speech perception: McGurk, phonemic restoration, VOT)
  - https://isle.hanover.edu/Chapter12.html
- Change blindness flicker demonstration
  - https://sites.socsci.uci.edu/~ddhoff/cb.html
- Michael Bach interactive phenomena library (assign specific stations)
  - https://michaelbach.de/ot/
  - https://michaelbach.de/ot/mot-adapt/
  - https://michaelbach.de/ot/mot-mib/

## Teaching design ideas
- 50-minute lab day: perception as inference
  - One ISLE Chapter 5 activity
  - One ISLE Chapter 7 activity
  - Change blindness demo
  - Submit a synthesis paragraph using two perception terms correctly
- Station rotation
  - ISLE 5, ISLE 7, ISLE 8, ISLE 12, change blindness (Bach stations optional)
- Submission pattern (scales well)
  - One screenshot per station
  - One prediction and one observation
  - One mechanism statement and one boundary-condition note

## Debrief prompts
- What did you perceive and how did it differ from the physical stimulus?
- What inference is the perceptual system making?
- What boundary condition changes the effect (fixation, distance, context cues)?
- What confound is most plausible in online perception demos?
- What conclusion is justified and what is overreach?
---
```

### Block 83 (lang=markdown | source=md | block 83)

```markdown
---
title: "PSY-132 Interactive Teaching Labs: Topics 10–12"
filename: "psy-132-topics-10-12-interactive-teaching-labs-free"
type: "resource_links_pack"
status: "curated"
created: "2026-01-11"
updated: "2026-01-11"
origin: "Combined pack of Topic 10 Learning, Topic 11 Memory, and Topic 12 Cognition interactive teaching lab link sets, constrained to free, student-facing, lab-style interactivity"
citation_style: "none"
verification_needed: true
tags:
  - "psy-132"
  - "interactive-labs"
  - "free"
  - "topics-10-12"
topics:
  - "Learning"
  - "Memory"
  - "Cognition"
aliases: []
sources:
  - "https://educationalgames.nobelprize.org/educational/medicine/pavlov/"
  - "https://educationalgames.nobelprize.org/educational/medicine/pavlov/pavlov.html"

  - "https://h5pstudio.ecampusontario.ca/"

  - "https://www.philosophyexperiments.com/wason/Default.aspx"
  - "https://montyhall.io/"
cssclasses: []
notes: "Pack includes Topic 10 Learning, Topic 11 Memory, Topic 12 Cognition. All activities are free and designed for lab-style teaching with debriefable outputs. Grade completion and methods reasoning, not performance level."
---

## Topic 10: Learning

## Lab set (free, lab-style)
- Nobel Prize Pavlov game (classical conditioning)
  - Hub: https://educationalgames.nobelprize.org/educational/medicine/pavlov/
  - Play: https://educationalgames.nobelprize.org/educational/medicine/pavlov/pavlov.html
  - Output: screenshot + CS/US/CR/UR + extinction or generalization prediction

- Rescorla–Wagner model (prediction error parameter lab)
  - Info: https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/rescrolawagner/
  - JS sim: https://psych.hanover.edu/JavaTest/CLE/Cognition_js/RescorlaWagner/
  - Output: two screenshots with one parameter change + model-based mechanism sentence

- LibreStudio H5P: Classical conditioning concept checks
  - 6.2A: https://studio.libretexts.org/h5p/15593
  - 6.2B: https://studio.libretexts.org/h5p/15594
  - 6.2D: https://studio.libretexts.org/h5p/15596
  - Output: completion screenshot + one justification sentence

- LibreStudio H5P: Operant conditioning concept checks
  - 6.3A: https://studio.libretexts.org/h5p/15599
  - 6.3B: https://studio.libretexts.org/h5p/15600
  - 6.3D: https://studio.libretexts.org/h5p/15602
  - Question Set 12.14A: https://studio.libretexts.org/h5p/5860
  - Output: completion screenshot + reinforcement/punishment label + increase/decrease statement

- eCampusOntario H5P schedules of reinforcement (Drag the Words)
  - https://h5pstudio.ecampusontario.ca/fr/content/64358
  - Output: completion screenshot + FR/VR/FI/VI examples

- Optional legacy shaping simulation (device-dependent)
  - ePsych Fuzz: https://epsych.msstate.edu/adaptive/Fuzz/index.html
  - Output: screenshot + “what I reinforced and what changed” + limitation statement

- LibreStudio H5P observational learning (modeling)
  - 6.4A: https://studio.libretexts.org/h5p/15603
  - Output: completion screenshot + attention/retention/reproduction/motivation list

## Teaching ideas
- Mechanisms lab day
  - Pavlov + Rescorla–Wagner + one operant H5P object
  - Deliverable: one-page learning audit (type, IV, DV, operational definition, one limitation)

---

## Topic 11: Memory

## Core lab hubs (free)
- PsyToolkit experiment library: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/
- Hanover Cognition Laboratory Experiments (HTML5/JS hub): https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/cognition.html
- TestMyBrain M2C2 Memory Games: https://studies.testmybrain.org/m2c2/?study=m2c2

## Lab set (free, lab-style)
- Working memory span (PsyToolkit run pages)
  - Digit Span: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_digitspan.html
  - Reverse Digit Span: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_rdigitspan.html
  - Corsi: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_corsi.html
  - Backward Corsi: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_backward_corsi.html
  - Output: one span score + screenshot + one confound statement

- Updating load (N-back)
  - 2-Back: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_nback2.html
  - Touch 2-Back: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/touch_nback2.html
  - Output: accuracy/summary + screenshot + speed–accuracy note

- Complex span (operation span)
  - https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_aospan.html
  - Output: score + screenshot + dual-task explanation

- Interference demonstration (Hanover)
  - Brown–Peterson: https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/BrownPeterson.html
  - Output: screenshot + decay vs interference sentence + limitation

- Serial position (Hanover)
  - https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/SerialPosition.html
  - Output: screenshot + primacy/recency interpretation + two derived values (early vs late)

- False memory (Hanover DRM)
  - https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/DRMfalseMemory.html
  - Output: screenshot + critical lure indicator + reconstruction explanation + ethics note

- Optional participation battery (TestMyBrain)
  - https://studies.testmybrain.org/m2c2/?study=m2c2
  - Output: completion screenshot + measurement-noise paragraph

## Teaching ideas
- “How memory fails” lab day
  - span + interference + false memory
  - Deliverable: one paragraph comparing three failure mechanisms

---

## Topic 12: Cognition

## Core lab hubs (free)
- PsyToolkit experiment library: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/
- Hanover Cognition Laboratory Experiments (HTML5/JS hub): https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/cognition.html

## Lab set (free, lab-style)
- Interference and control
  - PsyToolkit Stroop: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_stroop.html
  - Hanover Stroop: https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/stroop.html

- Distractor interference
  - PsyToolkit Flanker: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_flanker.html
  - Flanker arrows alt: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/flanker_arrows.html

- Flexibility and switching
  - Task switching: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_taskswitching.html
  - Multitasking: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_multitasking.html

- Inhibitory control
  - Go/No-go: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_go-no-go.html
  - Stop-signal: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_stopsignal.html

- Bottleneck demonstrations
  - Attentional blink (PsyToolkit): https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_ab.html
  - Attentional blink (Hanover): https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/attnBlink.html
  - Dual task (Hanover): https://psych.hanover.edu/javatest/cle/Cognition_js/exp/dualTask.html

- Visual search
  - PsyToolkit search: https://www.psytoolkit.org/experiment-library/experiment_search.html

- Reasoning and decision patterns
  - Wason tasks:
    - https://www.philosophyexperiments.com/wason/Default.aspx
    - https://www.philosophyexperiments.com/wason/Default2.aspx
    - https://www.philosophyexperiments.com/wason/Default3.aspx
  - Monty Hall simulator: https://montyhall.io/

## Teaching ideas
- “Where cognition breaks” lab day
  - Stroop or Flanker + task switching + Monty Hall
  - Deliverable: short synthesis identifying interference, capacity limits, and probabilistic reasoning

---
```
